Chapter 1 - GENERAL PROVISIONS 
 
Sec. 1-1. - How Code designated and cited. 
The ordinances embraced in the following chapters and sections shall constitute and be designated the "Code of Ordinances of the City of Canton, Mississippi," and may be so cited. 
State Law reference— Authority to revise, codify and publish ordinances, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 3374-76.  
Sec. 1-2. - Definitions and interpretation. 
In the construction of this Code, and of all ordinances, the following rules shall be observed, unless such construction would be inconsistent with the manifest intent of the mayor and board of aldermen: 
Board, board of aldermen. Whenever the term "board" or "board of aldermen" is used in this Code, it shall mean the Mayor and Board of Aldermen of the City of Canton, Mississippi. 
City. The words "the city" or "this city" shall be construed as if the words "of Canton, Mississippi" followed it. 
Computation of time. The time within which an act is to be done shall be computed by excluding the first and including the last day, and if the last day be Sunday or a legal holiday that day shall be excluded. 
Corporate limits, corporation limits, city limits. Whenever the words "corporate limits," "corporation limits," or "city limits" are used they shall mean the legal boundary of the City of Canton, Mississippi. 
County. Whenever the words "the county" or "this county" are used they shall mean the County of Madison, Mississippi. 
Delegation of authority. Whenever a provision appears requiring or authorizing the head of a department or agency of the city to do some act or make certain inspections, it shall be construed as authorizing the head of the department or agency to designate, delegate and authorize subordinates to perform the act or make the inspection unless the terms of the provision or section designate otherwise. 
Gender. A word importing the masculine gender only shall extend and be applied to females and to firms, partnerships and corporations as well as to males. 
Interpretation. In the interpretation and application of any provision of this Code, it shall be held to be the minimum requirements adopted for the promotion of the public health, safety, comfort, convenience and general welfare. Where any provision of the Code imposes greater restrictions upon the subject matter than the general provision imposed by the Code, the provision imposing the greater restriction or regulation shall be deemed to be controlling. 
Joint authority. All words giving a joint authority to three or more persons or officers shall be construed as giving such authority to a majority of such persons or officers. 
Keeper, proprietor. Whenever the word "keeper" or "proprietor" is used it shall mean persons, firms, associations, corporations, clubs and partnerships, whether acting by themselves or through a servant, agent or employee. 
Law. The term "law," when used in any ordinance, shall include any provision of the Constitution of the United States, or the State of Mississippi, and any statute of the United States or the State of Mississippi, and any ordinance, resolution or order of the mayor and board of aldermen of Canton, Mississippi. 
Month. Whenever the word "month" is used it shall mean a calendar month. 
Name of officer. Whenever the name of an officer is given it shall be construed as though the words "of the City of Canton" followed it. 
Nontechnical and technical words. Words and phrases shall be construed according to the common and approved usage of the language, but technical words and phrases and such others as may have acquired a peculiar and appropriate meaning in law shall be construed and understood according to such meaning. 
Number. Words used in the singular number only, either as descriptive of persons or things, shall extend to and embrace the plural number; and words used in the plural number shall extend to and embrace the singular number. 
Oath. The word "oath" shall include the word "affirmation" in all cases where by law an affirmation may be substituted for an oath. 
Offense. The term "offense" shall mean any violation of an ordinance liable to punishment by criminal prosecution. 
Or, and. "Or" may be read "and," and "and" may be read "or" if the sense requires it. 
Owner. Whenever the word "owner" is applied to a building or land, it shall include any part owner, joint owner, tenant in common, tenant in partnership, joint tenant or tenant by the entirety, of the whole or of a part of such building or land. 
Person. Whenever the word "person" is used it shall include, mean and be applied to any natural individual, firm, partnership, association, joint stock company, joint adventure, public or private corporation, or to a receiver, executor, trustee, conservator or other representative appointed by order of any court or in any other manner. 
Personal property. The term "personal property" shall include goods, chattels, effects, evidences of rights of action, and all written instruments by which any pecuniary obligation or any right, title or interest in any real or personal estate shall be created, acknowledged, transferred, incurred, defeated, discharged or diminished. 
Preceding, following. Whenever the words "preceding" and "following" are used they shall mean next before and next after, respectively. 
Premises. Whenever the word "premises" is used it shall mean place or places. 
Property. The term "property" includes personal property as defined herein and also every estate, interest or right in lands, tenements and hereditaments. 
Real property shall include every estate, interest or right, in lands, tenements and hereditaments. 
Residence. Whenever the word "residence" is used it shall mean the place adopted by a person as his place of habitation, and to which, whenever he is absent, he has the intention of returning. When a person eats at one place and sleeps at another, the place where such person sleeps shall be deemed his residence. 
Seal. Whenever the word "seal" is used it shall mean the city or corporate seal. 
Sidewalk. Whenever the word "sidewalk" is used it shall mean any portion of a street between the curbline, or the lateral lines of a roadway, and the adjacent property line, intended for the use of pedestrians, excluding parkways. 
Signature or subscription. The "signature" or "subscription" of a person includes a mark when the person cannot write. 
State. Whenever the words "the state" or "this state" are used they shall mean the State of Mississippi. 
Street. Whenever the word "street" is used it shall mean any street, avenue, boulevard, road, alley, lane, viaduct or other public highway in the city. 
Sworn. The term "sworn" shall include the word "affirmed," in all cases where by law an affirmation may be substituted for an oath. 
Tenant, occupant. Whenever the word "tenant" or "occupant" is applied to a building or land, it shall include any person holding a written or oral lease of, or who occupies the whole or a part of, such building or land, either alone or with others. 
Tense. Words used in the past or present tense include the future as well as the past and present. 
Week. Whenever the word "week" is used it shall mean seven days. 
Written, in writing may include printing, engraving, lithographing or any other representation of words, letters or figures; except that in all cases where the signature of any person is required, it shall always be the proper handwriting or mark of such person. 
Year. Whenever the word "year" is used it shall mean a calendar year. 
State Law reference— For definitions of terms used in statutes, see Miss. Code Ann. 1942, §§ 673—708.  
Sec. 1-3. - Altering Code. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to change or amend by additions or deletions any part or portion of this Code, or to insert or delete pages or portions thereof, or to alter or tamper with such Code in any manner whatsoever, which will cause the law of the City of Canton to be misrepresented thereby. Any person, firm or corporation violating this section shall be punished as provided in section 1-4 hereof.  
Sec. 1-4. - General penalty; continuing violations. 
Whenever in this Code or in any ordinance of the city any act is prohibited or is made or declared to be unlawful or an offense, or whenever in such Code or ordinance the doing of any act is required or the failure to do any act is declared to be unlawful, where no specific penalty is provided therefor, the violation of any such provision of this Code or any ordinance shall be punished by a fine not exceeding $500.00 or imprisonment for a term not exceeding 180 days, and the cost of prosecution, or by both such fine and imprisonment in the discretion of the municipal judge. Each day any violation of any provision of this Code or of any ordinance shall continue shall constitute a separate offense. 
In addition to the penalties hereinabove provided, any condition caused or permitted to exist in violation of any of the provisions of this Code or any ordinance shall be deemed a public nuisance and may be abated by the city, as provided by law, and each day that such condition continues shall be regarded as a new and separate offense. 
(Ord. of 6-7-83, §§ 1—3) 
Cross reference— Penalty for violation of local privilege tax code, § 18-17. 
State Law reference— Maximum punishment which may be imposed by a municipality, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 3374-137.  
Sec. 1-5. - Working city prisoners; credit against fine. 
(a)  Persons imprisoned for the violation of city ordinances may be required to work upon the streets, avenues and alleys of the city under the direction of the street commissioner. 
(b)  Where such prisoner is engaged in working out a fine assessed against him, he shall receive a credit against said fine at the rate of $3.00 per day worked. 
(c)  The street commissioner shall file a report with the jailer of each prisoner working out a fine, and the latter shall credit the result of such labor to the fine assessed against such prisoner as the same appears upon his jail docket. 
State Law reference— Credit against fines, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 7906.  
Sec. 1-6. - Custody of prisoners. 
All persons convicted of any violation of any ordinance of the city and sentenced to imprisonment for any period of time or being fined and in default of paying said fine and cost, shall be committed to prison until the payment of said fines and cost shall be made and remain in the custody of the chief of police and by him confined in such prison within the corporate limits as may be provided by the mayor and board of aldermen, or in the event the chief of police should have at any time any person so convicted and imprisoned in his custody, and for any cause there should fail to be a sufficient prison or jail provided by the mayor and board of aldermen for the safekeeping of said prisoner or prisoners, he may, with the consent of the mayor, make arrangements with the sheriff of Madison County for the safekeeping of said prisoner or prisoners, until the mayor and board of aldermen shall have provided a safe and sufficient prison for said prisoners.  
Sec. 1-7. - Amendments to Code—Effect. 
Any and all additions and amendments to this Code, when passed in such form as to indicate the intention of the mayor and board of aldermen to make the same a part hereof, shall be deemed to be incorporated in this Code so that reference to the "Code of the City of Canton, Mississippi," shall be understood and intended to include such additions and amendments.  
Sec. 1-8. - Same—Manner. 
All ordinances passed subsequent to the adoption of this Code which amend, repeal or in any way affect this Code may be numbered in accordance with the numbering system of this Code and printed for inclusion herein, or in the case of repealed chapters, sections and subsections or any part thereof, by subsequent ordinances, such repealed portions may be excluded from the Code by omission from reprinted pages affected thereby, and the subsequent ordinances as numbered and printed or omitted, in the case of repeal, shall be prima facie evidence of such subsequent ordinances until such time that this Code and subsequent ordinances numbered or omitted are readopted as a new Code of Ordinances by the mayor and board of aldermen.  
Sec. 1-9. - Same—Language. 
Amendments to any of the provisions of this Code should be made by amending such provisions by specific reference to the section of this Code in substantially the following language: 
"That section _______ of the Code of the City of Canton, Mississippi, is hereby amended to read as follows: … (Set out new provisions in full) …" 
State Law reference— Style of ordinance, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 3374-70.  
Sec. 1-10. - Same—New material. 
(a)  In the event a new section not heretofore existing in the Code is to be added, the following language may be used: 
"That the Code of the City of Canton, Mississippi, is hereby amended by adding a section (or article, chapter or other designation as the case may be), to be numbered _______, which reads as follows: … (Set out new provisions in full) …" 
(b)  In lieu of subsection (a) hereof, when the city council desires to enact an ordinance of a general and permanent nature embracing a subject not previously existing in the Code, which the council desires to incorporate into the Code, a provision in substantially the following language may be made part of such ordinance: 
"It is the intention of the mayor and board of aldermen, and it is hereby ordained, that the provisions of this ordinance shall become and be made part of the Code of the City of Canton, Mississippi, and the sections of this ordinance may be renumbered to accomplish such intention."  
Sec. 1-11. - Same—Repeal. 
All sections, articles, chapters or other provisions of this Code desired to be repealed should be specifically repealed by section number, article number, chapter or other number, as the case may be.  
Sec. 1-12. - Same—Subject to general penalty. 
In case of the amendment by the city council of any section of this Code for which a penalty is not provided, the general penalty as provided in section 1-4 of this Code shall apply to the section as amended; or in case such amendment contains provisions for which a penalty, other than the aforementioned general penalty is provided in another section in the same chapter, the penalty so provided in such other section shall be held to relate to the section so amended, unless such penalty is specifically repealed therein.  
Sec. 1-13. - Catchlines of sections. 
The catchlines of the several sections of this Code printed in boldface type are intended as mere catchwords to indicate the contents of the section and shall not be deemed or taken to be titles of such sections, nor as any part of the section, nor, unless expressly so provided, shall they be so deemed when any of such sections including the catchlines, are amended or reenacted.  
Sec. 1-14. - Effect of repeal of ordinances. 
The repeal of an ordinance shall not revive any ordinances in force before or at the time the ordinance repealed took effect. 
The repeal of an ordinance shall not affect any punishment or penalty incurred before the repeal took effect, nor any suit, prosecution or proceeding pending at the time of the repeal, for an offense committed under the ordinance repealed.  
Sec. 1-15. - Severability of parts of Code. 
It is hereby declared to be the intention of the board of mayor and aldermen that the sections, paragraphs, sentences, clauses and phrases of this Code are severable, and if any phrase, clause, sentence, paragraph or section of this Code shall be declared unconstitutional, invalid or unenforceable by the valid judgment or decree of a court of competent jurisdiction, such unconstitutionality, invalidity or unenforceability shall not affect any of the remaining phrases, clauses, sentences, paragraphs and sections of this Code.

Chapter 2 - ADMINISTRATION[1]

State Law reference— Municipalities generally, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 3374-01 et seq. 
 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Sec. 2-1. - Seal. 
The seal of the city shall be a compression seal consisting of two concentric circles, between the circumferences of which and at the top appear the words: "Clerk of City of Canton," and at the bottom the words: "Madison County, Miss.," and in the center of the inner circle a coat of arms in the likeness of the "American Eagle." ;hn0; (Code 1930, § 319)  
Sec. 2-2. - Availability of funds for payment. 
All monies of the city held by the depository shall be subject to payment upon demand by the city clerk, on his warrant, issued on the order of the mayor and board of aldermen, countersigned by the mayor. 
(Code 1930, § 98) 
State Law reference— Duties of city depository, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 3374-102; depositories generally, § 9170 et seq.  
Sec. 2-3. - Human cultural needs department. 
(a)  Created. A human cultural needs department of the city, is hereby created. 
(b)  Director and employees. The department shall consist of a director and any other persons as be required in the judgment of the mayor and board of aldermen and to fix and pay their compensation from funds available to the city therefor. 
(c)  Responsibilities and duties. The human cultural needs department shall have and exercise such of the powers and authority as may be prescribed by the guidelines, orders, resolutions and ordinances of the mayor and board of aldermen, to attend to housing and housing needs related issues involving the citizenry of Canton, Mississippi; transportation; community and economic needs; crime prevention; the promotion and development of cultural and artistic events, and public works need of and for all the citizens of Canton, Mississippi. 
In addition, the human cultural needs department shall, subject to the supervision and control of the mayor and board of aldermen, act in conjunction with and interface with all existing and hereafter created departments of the city, including programs and activities sponsored by or under the auspices of the city and to act in conjunction with and to interface with county, state and national agencies and institutions in promoting, implementing and establishing programs, activities and/or agencies as well as applying for such grants as said department may be eligible to receive and which are designed to create, promote and improve the cultural needs of the city. 
(Ord. of 9-15-98, §§ 1—3) 
Editor's note— An ordinance adopted Sept. 15, 1998, §§ 1—3, did not specifically amend the Code; therefore, inclusion as § 2-3 was at the discretion of the editor.  
Sec. 2-4. - City wage requirements. 
Effective fiscal year 2016 (which is October 1, 2015 on the calendar year), minimum hourly wage for city employees shall be $9.75. Each city employee shall be compensated at a rate of pay not less than the minimum hourly wage in effect, as set forth by this section. 
(Ord. of 3-17-15) 
Editor's note— An ordinance adopted March 17, 2015, did not specify manner of inclusion; hence, inclusion as section 2-4 is at the discretion of the editor.  
Secs. 2-5—2-17. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - GOVERNING BODY  
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
 
Sec. 2-18. - Regular meetings. 
The mayor and board of aldermen of the city shall conduct regular meetings on the first and third Tuesdays of each month commencing at 4:30 p.m. in the Canton City Hall located at 226 East Peace Street, Canton, Mississippi. 
(Ord. of 12-2-69, §§ 1, 2; Ord. of 9-16-75, § 1; Ord. of 8-7-79, § 1; Ord. of 2-19-80, § 1 Ord. of 10-4-94; Ord. of 6-20-95; Ord. of 8-19-97; Ord. of 3-3-98; Ord. of 6-4-02; Ord. of 8-1-17) 
State Law reference— Regular meetings, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 3374-43.  
Sec. 2-19. - Recessed meetings. 
The mayor and board of aldermen may recess any regular meeting from time to time to convene on a day fixed by an order of the mayor and board of aldermen entered on its minutes and may transact any business coming before it for consideration. 
(Ord. of 12-2-69, § 3)  
Sec. 2-20. - Special meetings. 
Special meetings of the mayor and board of aldermen may be held at the discretion of the mayor, or at the written request of two members of the board. 
(Code 1930, § 61) 
State Law reference— Special meetings, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 3374-44.  
Sec. 2-21. - Quorum. 
In all cases, it shall require a majority of all the aldermen elected to constitute a quorum for the transaction of business. 
(Ord. of 12-2-69, § 4)  
Sec. 2-22. - Rules of order. 
Robert's Rules of Order, Newly Revised, copyright 1970, published by Scott, Foresman and Company, shall govern the mayor and board of aldermen in its deliberation in cases not otherwise provided for by statute, ordinance, rule or regulation.  
Secs. 2-23—2-27. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 2. - MAYOR[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference— Bond of mayor, § 2-61; civil emergency curfew, § 22-100 et seq. 
State Law reference— Duties generally, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 3374-40 et seq. 
 
Sec. 2-28. - Generally. 
(a)  The mayor shall have the superintending control of all the officers, employees and affairs of the city and shall take care that the laws and ordinances of the city are enforced and executed. 
(b)  The position of mayor will, from and after the effective date of this subsection, require the full-time service of the mayor. 
(Ord. of 5-4-82, § 1) 
Editor's note— At the discretion of the editor, § 1 of an ordinance of May 4, 1982, has been included as hereinabove set out in subsection (b) of § 2-28. The provisions are effective from and after one month from May 4, 1982.  
Sec. 2-29. - Compensation. 
The annual compensation for the mayor of the city, shall be $60,000.00, plus benefits to be paid in 26 equal installments, with the first year to be paid on a pro rata basis. 
(Ord. of 11-6-79, Ord. of 6-16-81; Ord. of 5-4-82, § 2; Ord. of 5-28-85, § 2; Ord. of 12-7-99, § 1; Ord. of 10-16-01, § 1; Ord. of 2-19-08; Ord. of 3-3-08, § 1)  
Secs. 2-30—2-34. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 3. - BOARD OF ALDERMEN 
 
Sec. 2-35. - Composition, manner of election. 
The board of aldermen shall be composed of seven members, one elected from each of the wards of the city, who shall be a resident of the ward from which elected, and one elected from the city at large. 
(Code 1930, § 497; Ord. of 1-6-42; Ord. of 12-19-72, § 1; Ord. of 10-3-78, § 8) 
Cross reference— Elections, Ch. 10; wards, § 10-35 et seq. 
State Law reference— Number of aldermen, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 3374-36.  
Sec. 2-36. - Attend meetings. 
The aldermen shall attend all regular meetings and all special meetings lawfully called of the mayor and board of aldermen. 
(Code 1930, § 8; Ord. of 8-20-68, § 1)  
Sec. 2-37. - Compensation. 
The annual compensation for the aldermen of the city, shall be $23,000.00, plus benefits to be paid in 26 equal installments, with the first year to be paid on a pro rata basis. 
(Ord. of 11-6-79; Ord. of 5-28-85, § 1; Ord. of 1-7-02, § 1; Ord. of 2-19-08; Ord. of 3-3-08, § 2) 
Editor's note— Ord. of Nov. 6, 1979, paragraph (B), has been treated as superseding the provisions of former § 2-37, also pertaining to compensation for the board of aldermen, which derived from Code 1930, §§ 8, 9; Ord. of Aug. 4, 1942, § 1 and Ord. of Aug. 20, 1968, § 1.  
Secs. 2-38—2-47. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE III. - OFFICERS[3] 
Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
Cross reference— Civil defense director, § 9-3; health officer, § 15-2; chief of police, § 27-18 et seq.; traffic engineer, § 33-5. 
 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
 
Sec. 2-48. - Generally. 
The mayor and board of aldermen shall appoint and employ such officers and employees as may be required by the provisions of this Code, state law and city ordinances and as may be required for the proper and efficient conduct of the business and operation of the city.  
Sec. 2-49. - Terms. 
Every officer or employee of the city, unless otherwise specifically provided, shall serve at the pleasure of the mayor and board of aldermen.  
Sec. 2-50. - Compensation. 
The compensation of each officer and employee of this city shall be as provided by state law, this Code or city ordinance.  
Sec. 2-51. - Oath of office. 
All officers shall take the following oath before entering upon the duties of their office: 
"I, _______, do solemnly swear (or affirm) that I will faithfully support and bear true allegiance to the Constitution of the United States and the State of Mississippi and obey the laws thereof; that I am not disqualified from holding office by the Constitutions of the United States or the State of Mississippi, that I will support and obey the laws, ordinances and resolutions of the Mayor and Board of Aldermen of the City of Canton, and that I will faithfully discharge the duties of the office on which I am about to enter. So help me God." 
The oath, with official bond, when approved, shall be filed with the city clerk. 
(Code 1930, § 232)  
Sec. 2-52. - Books subject to inspection. 
Every officer or employee of the city shall at all times, when requested, submit his books and official papers to the inspection of the mayor, or any alderman, or to any person or committee appointed or authorized by the mayor and board of aldermen to examine the same and to the public for examination and inspection. 
(Code 1930, § 228)  
Sec. 2-53. - Books, etc., to successor. 
Every officer or employee of the city, on going out of office, shall deliver to his successor or to the mayor all books, tools, instruments and everything pertaining to his office and is entitled to a receipt therefor if requested. 
(Code 1930, § 228)  
Sec. 2-54. - Not to speculate in warrants. 
No officer or employee of the city shall purchase or sell any city script or warrants on speculation; and no officer shall loan out or use on his own account, on any pretext, any money of the city in his hands or on any pretext, pledge or loan any of the property, notes, bonds, or other securities of the city, except as ordered by the mayor and aldermen; and the doing of these things is hereby declared sufficient cause for removal. 
(Code 1930, § 231)  
Sec. 2-55. - Causes for removal. 
Every officer or employee who shall refuse or wilfully neglect to perform the duties imposed upon him by law, this Code or ordinance or who shall in his official acts be guilty of any fraud, extortion, oppression, or favoritism or wilful injustice, or for any satisfactory cause, shall be removed from office. 
(Code 1930, § 230)  
Secs. 2-56—2-60. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 2. - BONDS 
 
Sec. 2-61. - Required. 
The following officers of this city shall post bond payable to the state in the following penal sums with surety by one or more guaranty or surety companies authorized to do business in this state, and such bonds shall remain in full force and effect during their respective terms of office: 
Mayor ..... $10,000.00 
City clerk, assessor and collector ..... 10,000.00 
Chief of police ..... 5,000.00 
Superintendent of public works ..... 5,000.00 
All other officers and employees ..... 2,500.00 
(Ord. of 12-2-69, § 1)  
Sec. 2-62. - Payment of premiums. 
The premiums on the bonds required by this division shall be paid from the general fund and the city clerk is hereby authorized, empowered and directed to pay the same by warrant drawn thereon as and when due and payable. 
(Ord. of 12-2-69, § 4)  
Sec. 2-63. - Condition. 
The bonds of all officers and employees required to give bond shall be conditioned on the faithful performance of all the duties of such office during his continuance therein. 
(Ord. of 12-2-69, § 2)  
Sec. 2-64. - Approval, recording. 
The bonds required by this division shall be approved by the mayor and city clerk, shall be filed with the city clerk, who shall keep the same as a permanent record in his office, and in addition thereto shall record the same in the office of the chancery clerk of the county. 
(Ord. of 12-2-69, § 3)  
Secs. 2-65—2-69. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 3. - CITY CLERK 
 
Sec. 2-70. - Appointment. 
The board of aldermen, by a majority vote thereof, the mayor voting in case of a tie vote, shall appoint a city clerk for the city. Such appointment shall be in writing, signed by the mayor and attested by the clerk. 
(Ord. of 7-6-65, §§ 2, 3) 
Cross reference— Bond of clerk, § 2-61.  
Sec. 2-71. - Combination of offices. 
The office of city clerk is hereby combined with the office of city tax collector and city tax assessor, and the appointee to the office of city clerk shall also serve in each of such capacities, for which the mayor and board of aldermen may allow additional compensation to be paid. 
(Ord. of 7-6-65, § 4)  
Sec. 2-72. - Reserved. 
Editor's note— An ordinance adopted Nov. 15, 1994, repealed § 2-72, which pertained to qualifications and derived from § 2 of an ordinance adopted July 6, 1965.  
Sec. 2-73. - Term. 
The city clerk shall serve in each of the capacities to which appointed at the pleasure of the mayor and board of aldermen and may be discharged by such governing authorities at any time, either with or without cause; provided, however, that the term of office of the city clerk shall expire at the expiration of the term of office of the board of aldermen making the appointment, unless sooner discharged as herein provided. 
(Ord. of 7-6-65, § 7)  
Sec. 2-74. - Compensation. 
Upon making the appointment of the clerk, the mayor and board of aldermen shall fix and establish the compensation to be paid to the clerk. 
(Ord. of 7-6-65, § 2)  
Sec. 2-75. - Duties generally. 
The duties of the city clerk, including the office of city tax collector and tax assessor shall be those now prescribed by state law, the provisions of this Code and the ordinances of the city in addition to such other duties as the mayor and board of aldermen may from time to time prescribe. 
(Ord. of 7-6-65, § 5) 
Cross reference— Clerk as registrar of voters, § 10-17 et seq.  
Sec. 2-76. - Reserved. 
Editor's note— An ordinance adopted June 20, 1995, repealed § 2-76, which pertained to clerk of utilities commission and derived from Code 1930, § 90; and § 1 of an ordinance adopted June 6, 1950.  
Secs. 2-77—2-81. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 4. - CITY ATTORNEY 
 
Sec. 2-82. - Appointment. 
The board of aldermen, by a majority vote thereof, the mayor voting in case of a tie vote, shall appoint a city attorney for the city. Such appointment shall be in writing, signed by the mayor and attested by the clerk.  
Sec. 2-83. - Compensation. 
Upon making the appointment of the attorney, the mayor and board of aldermen shall fix and establish the compensation to be paid to the attorney.  
Sec. 2-84. - General duties. 
The city attorney shall give legal advice to the mayor and board of aldermen and represent the city in all civil and criminal cases. 
(Code 1930, § 217; Ord. of 2-6-45)  
Sec. 2-85. - Attend meetings. 
The city attorney shall attend all of the meetings of the mayor and board of aldermen. 
(Code 1930, § 217; Ord. of 2-6-45)  
Secs. 2-86—2-90. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 5. - CHIEF ADMINISTRATIVE OFFICER[4] 

Footnotes:

Sec. 2-91. - Creation. 
The City of Canton now finds it in the best interest of the city to create and establish the position of chief administrative officer (CAO) for the administrative term beginning in 2021. 
(Ord. of 3-20-18)  
Sec. 2-92. - Qualifications; compensation. 
The CAO shall be a full time employee of the municipality and shall serve at the discretion of the mayor and board of aldermen, and shall receive such compensation as the mayor and board of aldermen may determine. 
The CAO shall be chosen solely on the basis of experience and administrative qualifications. 
(Ord. of 3-20-18)

Footnotes:

State Law reference— Public employee's retirement system, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 7446-01 et seq. 
 
Sec. 2-106. - Extension of benefits. 
It is hereby declared to be the policy and purpose of the city to extend the provisions of Articles 1 and 11, Senate Bill No. 273, Regular Session, Mississippi Legislature of 1952, providing social security and state retirement to eligible employees and officers of this city. In pursuance of said policy, and for that purpose, the officers of the city shall take such action as may be required by applicable state or federal laws or regulations. 
(Ord. of 8-5-52, § 1)  
Sec. 2-107. - Execution of agreements. 
The mayor and city clerk are hereby authorized and directed to execute an agreement with the state public employees' retirement system to secure coverage of eligible employees as provided in this division. 
(Ord. of 8-5-52, § 2)  
Sec. 2-108. - Withholdings authorized. 
Withholdings from salaries or wages of employees for the purposes provided in this division are hereby authorized to be made in the amounts and at such time as may be required by applicable state and federal laws and regulations, and shall be paid over to the state agency in such amount and at such times as are designated by state laws and regulations. 
(Ord. of 8-5-52, § 3)

Employer contributions and administrative expense shall be paid to the state agency in accordance with applicable state laws and regulations from amount appropriated for such purposes. 
(Ord. of 8-5-52, § 4)  
Sec. 2-110. - Records, reports. 
The city clerk shall maintain such records and submit such reports relative to the provisions of this division as may be required by applicable state and federal laws or regulations. 
(Ord. of 8-5-52, § 5)

ARTICLE V. - PERSONNEL POLICIES AND PROCEDURES[6] 

Footnotes: 
--- (6) --- 
Editor's note— An ordinance of December 4, 1984, §§ 1—4, did not specifically amend the Code; therefore, inclusion as § 2-161 was at the discretion of the editor. 
 
Sec. 2-161. - Adopted. 
(a)  The personnel policies and procedures are hereby adopted by reference and enacted as the official "Personnel Policies and Procedures of the City of Canton, Mississippi," and shall be treated and considered as new and original comprehensive personnel policies and procedures which shall supercede all other personnel policies and procedures duly adopted and enacted by the mayor and board of aldermen on or before the fourth day of December, 1984. 
(b)  All the provisions of the personnel policies and procedures shall be in full force and effect on and after the seventh day of January, 1985. 
(c)  Any and all additions or amendments to such personnel policies and procedures, when passed in such form as to indicate the intention of the city to make the same a part thereof, shall be deemed incorporated into such personnel policies and procedures, so that referenced to the personnel policies and procedures of the City of Canton, Mississippi, shall be understood and intended to include such additions and amendments. 
(d)  A copy of the personnel policies and procedures, certified to by the mayor and city clerk shall be on file at the time of the adoption of the personnel policies and procedures and shall be kept on file in the office of the city clerk. It shall be the express duty of the city clerk or someone so authorized to insert in the designated places all amendments or ordinances which indicate the intention of the city to make the same a part of such personnel policies and procedures when the same shall be printed or reprinted in page form, and to extract from said personnel policies and procedures all provisions which may from time to time be repealed. This copy of the personnel policies and procedures shall be available to all persons desiring to examine the same and shall be considered the official personnel policies and procedures of the City of Canton, Mississippi. 
(Ord. of 12-4-84, §§ 1—4)  
Chapter 3 - ADVERTISING AND SIGNS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Pulling down lawful advertisements, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 2003; untrue, false and misleading advertising, § 2003.5; construction, erection of billboards, § 2021. 
 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Sec. 3-1. - Posting on trees, poles prohibited. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to post, tack, nail, attach or in any other manner fasten signs, bills, circulars, posters, notices, papers or other advertising matter of any description or kind to any telephone, telegraph or electric light pole or upon any tree standing or growing upon any of the streets or public grounds of the city. 
(Code 1930, § 195)  
Secs. 3-2—3-16. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - DISTRIBUTION OF HANDBILLS[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference— Littering generally, § 14-2 et seq. 
 
Sec. 3-17. - Definitions. 
For the purposes of this article, the following words and phrases shall have the meanings respectively ascribed to them: 
Handbill. Any printed or written matter, any sample or device, dodger, circular, leaflet, pamphlet, paper, booklet or any other printed or otherwise reproduced original or copies of any matter of literature. 
Newspaper. Any newspaper of general circulation as defined by general law, any newspaper duly entered with the post office department of the United States, in accordance with federal statute or regulation, and any newspaper filed and recorded with any recording officer as provided by general law; and in addition thereto, shall mean and include any periodical or current magazine regularly published with not less than four issues per year, and sold to the public, and shall mean and include any other copyrighted material. 
Vehicle. Every device in, upon or by which any person or property is or may be transported or drawn upon a highway, including devices used exclusively upon stationary rails or tracks.  
Sec. 3-18. - Exemption for mail and newspapers. 
The provisions of this article shall not apply to the distribution of mail by the United States, nor to newspapers, except that newspapers shall be placed on private property in such a manner as to prevent their being carried or deposited by the elements upon any street, sidewalk or other public place or upon private property. 
(Ord. of 1-21-64, § 1)  
Sec. 3-19. - Permit required. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to deliver, hand out, distribute or otherwise circulate, except by United States Postal Service, or to cause to be delivered, handed out, distributed or otherwise circulated, except by United States Postal Service, any handbill, circular, poster, pamphlet or similar written matter upon any municipal street, sidewalk or in any public place within the city without obtaining a permit therefor. 
(Ord. of 1-21-64, § 1)  
Sec. 3-20. - Application for permit. 
Any person desiring to deliver, hand out, distribute or otherwise circulate any handbill, circular, poster, pamphlet or similar written material upon any municipal street, sidewalk or other public place within the city, shall first make application in writing, with a copy of the proposed handbill, circular, poster or pamphlet to be distributed or circulated attached thereto, to the mayor and the clerk for permission so to do; and the mayor and chief of police are hereby authorized and empowered to consider and act upon said application, and to either grant or deny the permit applied for. The decision of the mayor and chief of police in regard to the same shall be final. 
(Ord. of 1-21-64, § 2)  
Sec. 3-21. - Inhabited private premises. 
No person shall throw, deposit or distribute any handbill in or upon private premises which are inhabited, except by handing or transmitting any such handbill directly to the owner, occupant or other person then present in or upon such private premises. Provided, however, that in case of inhabited private premises which are not posted, such person, unless requested by anyone upon such premises not to do so, may place or deposit any such handbill in or upon such premises if such handbill is so placed or deposited as to secure or prevent such handbill from being blown or drifted about such premises or sidewalks, streets or other public places, and except that mailboxes may not be so used when so prohibited by federal postal law or regulation.  
Sec. 3-22. - Prohibited where properly posted. 
No person shall throw, deposit or distribute any handbill upon any private premises, if requested by anyone thereon not to do so, or if there is placed on such premises a sign bearing the words: "No Trespassing," "No Peddlers or Agents," "No Advertisement," or any similar notice, indicating in any manner that the occupants of such premises do not wish to have their right of privacy disturbed, or to have any handbills left upon such premises.  
Sec. 3-23. - Depositing on uninhabited or vacant premises. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to throw or deposit any handbill in or upon any private premises which is uninhabited or vacant.  
Sec. 3-24. - Placing on vehicles. 
No person shall throw or deposit any handbill in or upon any vehicle. 
Cross reference— Motor vehicles generally, Ch. 20.  
Sec. 3-25. - Restricted in public places. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to hand out or distribute or sell any handbill in any public place; except that a handbill may be personally delivered to any person willing to accept the same.  
Secs. 3-26—3-40. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE III. - SIGNS[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
Editor's note— An ordinance of December 2, 1985, §§ 1—10, did not specifically amend the Code; therefore, inclusion as §§ 3-41 through 3-52 was at the discretion of the editor. The effective date of this article shall be December 2, 1985. 
Cross reference— Zoning, App. A. 
 
Sec. 3-41. - General application of regulations. 
The regulations set forth shall apply and govern in all zoning districts except as hereinafter provided. No sign or outdoor advertising device shall be erected or retained unless it is in compliance with the regulations for the district in which it is located. No sign or other outdoor advertising device shall be erected or maintained in operation which constitutes a nuisance by reason of light, glare, noise, animation or flashing in any zoning district. No illumination is to unduly disturb the use of residential districts, and property therein. 
(Ord. of 12-2-85, § 1)  
Sec. 3-42. - Accessory uses. 
Any sign placed on land or on a structure for the purpose of identification, protection or for advertising a product or service available on the premises, or use conducted thereon shall be deemed to be an accessory use. It is the purpose of this article to place such limitations on the display of all said signs as will assure that they will: (a) be appropriate to the land, building, or use to which they are appurtenant, and (b) be adequate but not excessive for the intended purpose of identification, protection, or advertisement. Signs advertising uses are specifically intended, among other things, to avoid excessive competition among sign displays in their demand for public attention. 
(Ord. of 12-2-85, § 2)  
Sec. 3-43. - Permits. 
A sign permit shall be obtained from the zoning administrator before any sign or advertising structure is erected, displayed, replaced or altered so as to change its overall dimension. 
(Ord. of 12-2-85, § 3)  
Sec. 3-44. - Signs in all districts. 
The following signs shall be permitted and sign regulations shall apply in all districts: 
(1)  In determining the square foot area of any sign or other outdoor advertising display, the measurement shall include the entire display together with any lattice work, fencing or wall work, incidental to its ornamentation. 
(2)  Directional signs not exceeding two square feet may be erected provided they are not within the right-of-way of any street. 
(3)  Bulletin boards not over 12 square feet in area for public, charitable or religious institutions shall be allowed when located on the premises of said institution. 
(4)  Temporary signs advertising property for sale, rent, lease or trade provided such signs shall be no wider than six feet. 
(5)  Signs not over 12 square feet in area denoting architect, contractor or engineer shall be allowed when placed upon construction sites during actual construction. 
(6)  Signs of public service companies indicating danger and aids to service or safety. 
(7)  No sign shall be permitted on that part of the side or rear wall of a building within 100 feet from any residential district. 
(8)  Every sign pertaining to a particular use shall be deemed to be accessory to that use, and, if such use ceases, shall be removed not more than six months thereafter, provided that: (a) Real estate "sold" sign shall be removed 30 days after replacement on the property; and (b) Temporary signs, such as political campaign signs and those related to temporary uses such as a fair or carnival shall be removed within five days after the last day of the event to which they pertain. Signs hereafter erected on public lands contrary to the provisions of this code are subject to immediate removal. 
(Ord. of 12-2-85, § 4)  
Sec. 3-45. - Signs in residential district. 
Small professional or announcement signs of profession or businesses permitted shall be allowed in these districts. However, such signs shall not exceed one and one-half square feet in area. 
(Ord. of 12-2-85, § 5)  
Sec. 3-46. - Signs in commercial districts. 
The following signs shall be permitted and sign regulations shall apply in all commercial districts. 
(1)  The maximum aggregate area of all signs shall be one square foot of sign area for each foot of width of the front wall of the building. 
(2)  Additionally, one sign, not exceeding six square feet in area, may be erected to identify secondary entrances to a building from a pedestrian way from an alley, or from automobile parking space. 
(Ord. of 12-2-85, § 6)  
Sec. 3-47. - Signs in industrial districts. 
The maximum aggregate area for all signs shall be three square feet for each foot of width of the front wall of the building. 
(Ord. of 12-2-85, § 7)  
Sec. 3-48. - Outdoor advertising signs. 
The following regulations shall apply to outdoor advertising signs. 
(1)  Outdoor advertising of a permanent nature shall be classified as an industrial use and shall be permitted only in the industrial districts. Such signs shall not exceed 100 square feet in the industrial districts (including structural support and apron). 
(2)  Outdoor advertising signs shall not be erected, placed or hung nearer to the street right-of-way line upon which said display faces than the building setback lines provided for in the district or 50 feet, whichever is greater. 
(3)  Outdoor advertising signs shall be at least 2,000 feet apart on the same side of any arterial street, collector street, local street or highway. The distance between said signs shall be measured along the nearest edge of pavement between points directly opposite the signs. Each side of the street will be measured separately. 
(4)  Outdoor advertising signs shall be limited to one sign per facing and may be erected in a v-shaped pattern or may be erected back-to-back on the same supports. 
(5)  Outdoor advertising signs located along the interstate highways shall conform with the provisions of the Federal Highway Beautification Act of 1965 as enacted by the State of Mississippi, except that where the requirements of this article are greater, the latter shall govern. 
(Ord. of 12-2-85, § 8)  
Sec. 3-49. - Legal nonconforming signs. 
(a)  Within the categories identified by this article, it is recognized that there exist permanent signs and/or sign structures which were lawful before this article was adopted, but which would now be prohibited under the terms of this article. To eliminate unnecessary, undue hardship in such cases, it is the intent of this article to permit these nonconforming permanent signs to continue until they are removed, abandoned or destroyed, but not to encourage their survival. Such permanent nonconforming sign or sign structure lawful before the adoption of this article may continue to be used as long as it is adequately maintained and does not constitute a public hazard or nuisance, and provided that it is not expanded, extended, enlarged or changed in basic structural design and integrity, height or area. 
(b)  A permanent nonconforming sign shall not be changed to another nonconforming use. Nothing in this article shall prevent the strengthening or restoring to a safe condition of any portion of a sign or structure declared unsafe by proper authority. Such signs may be improved only to the extent that such improvement does not exceed 50 percent of the current market value of the existing structure. 
(Ord. of 12-2-85, § 9)  
Sec. 3-50. - Termination of nonconforming sign structures. 
(a)  Any permanent nonconforming sign or sign structure which is partially destroyed or damaged by fire, accident or natural cause beyond 50 percent of its current market value shall thereafter be removed or reconstructed in conformance to the regulations of this article. 
(b)  Any permanent nonconforming sign or sign structure which is improved or altered to comply with the provisions of this article shall thereafter be considered as conforming. 
(c)  Any permanent nonconforming use of signs which was lawful before the adoption of this article may be continued, and provided further that these regulations shall not be construed to require a change in plans, construction or designated use of any sign upon which construction and/or other improvements were lawfully begun prior to the effective date of adoption of this article. 
(d)  Any permanent nonconforming sign, so designated due to the zoning classification of the use of property on which it is located, which ceases to be used as such for a period of more than six consecutive months, shall subsequently conform to the regulations of this article. 
(Ord. of 12-2-85, § 9)  
Sec. 3-51. - Abandoned signs. 
Any sign which is found in Canton to be abandoned or is in such state of disrepair so as to be considered an unsightly nuisance, or signs which no longer serve any useful purpose for the owner or the advertiser thereon, shall be prohibited and subject to immediate removal. The zoning administrator shall notify the owner of any such abandoned, unsightly or useless sign, if the owner is known to this responsible officer, and demand the immediate removal of said sign; if after six months from the date of said notice, the sign has not been removed, then the zoning administrator shall have authority to effect immediate removal of said sign with the cost of said removal being assessed against the owner of the sign if known, and no liability shall attach to the city, its officials or agents for said removal of such a public nuisance. 
(Ord. of 12-2-85, § 9)  
Sec. 3-52. - Identification signs and markers. 
Nothing contained herein shall be construed to prohibit the use of identification signs and markers including those used at the entrances to subdivisions, apartments and townhouse complexes so long as they or properly maintained, providing that in each situation they do not have a surface area in excess of 30 square feet. 
(Ord. of 12-2-85, § 10)  
Chapter 4 - ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Driving while intoxicated, § 33-247. 
State Law reference— Alcoholic beverages, Miss. Code Ann. 1943, § 10265-01 et seq.; regulations as to intoxicating liquors, § 2612 et seq. 
 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Sec. 4-1. - Purpose. 
This chapter is adopted for the purpose of supplementing the rules and regulations promulgated by the Mississippi State Tax Commission under the provisions of House Bill 112 of the Regular Legislative Session of 1966, in order to promote the common good and the general welfare of the citizens of the city.  
Sec. 4-2. - Conformance to state law, regulations. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to sell or offer for sale, or otherwise dispense alcoholic beverages of any kind, or to have such in his or her possession within the city in violation of any of the terms and provisions of any statute of the state or in violation of any rules and regulations promulgated by the state tax commission.  
Sec. 4-3. - Retail outlets—Application of zoning ordinance. 
The zoning ordinance of the city, together with the off-street parking regulations, shall apply to retail outlets for the sale of alcoholic beverages, as such term is defined by Section 10265-05 of the Mississippi Code of 1942, Recompiled. 
Cross reference— Zoning ordinance, App. A.  
Sec. 4-4. - Same—Application of technical provisions; location restrictions. 
All of the applicable provisions of the building code, the fire prevention code, the electrical code, the plumbing and the gas codes adopted by this Code shall control the location, construction, use and operation of package stores and other liquor outlets. 
No permits or approvals of use and occupancy under said codes or other ordinances and regulations of the city shall be issued approving the location, construction, use or operation of package stores or other liquor outlets until the expiration of seven days after the last publication, as required by the statutes of the state and rules of the state tax commission. 
If, in the event written objection is received by the city clerk prior to the expiration of said seven day period, which is made by a person owning land or real property, or having business interests operating within a radius of 160 feet of the applicant's proposed retail outlet, then no such permit or other approval of the use and occupancy of said outlet shall be issued unless authorized by the mayor and board of aldermen. As soon as possible after the filing of such objection, but no later than 21 days from such filing, a hearing shall be held by the mayor and board of aldermen. At such hearing the objector shall have the burden of showing that the granting of such permit or approval of use and occupancy shall be contrary to the public health, morals and safety. Provided, however, that said permit or approval shall be issued unless the mayor and board of aldermen affirmatively find that the operation of said retail outlet would adversely affect the public health, morals and safety, giving reasonable consideration to the effect of said schools, churches and other such institutions within the immediate area. Provided, however, no retail outlet shall be deemed to have an effect on any such school, church or other institution if more than 400 feet away from same, or more than 100 feet away from same in a commercial zoned district. 
Cross reference— Building, Ch. 7; electricity, Ch. 11; plumbing and gas, Ch. 26.  
Sec. 4-5. - Same—Rear door. 
The rear door, if any, to any building where intoxicating beverages are stored or dispensed shall be equipped with a lock so that the same cannot be opened from the outside without the use of a key which shall be kept at all times by the owner or operator thereof, and further equipped with a panic device so that the same may be readily opened from the interior of the building.  
Sec. 4-6. - Same—Payment of privilege tax. 
Prior to the beginning of the operation of any package store or other outlet for the sale of intoxicating beverages where a privilege tax is required, the owner or operator thereof shall produce and exhibit to the city tax collector evidence of payment of the same. 
Cross reference— Local privilege tax, § 18-16 et seq.  
Sec. 4-7. - Hours of operation. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to sell, give away or otherwise dispense at any place where alcoholic beverages are sold any alcoholic beverages between the hours of 1:00 a.m. and 7:00 a.m. 
(Ord. of 8-2-05) 
State Law reference— Similar state law, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 10265-32(c).  
Sec. 4-8. - Emergency closure of places where sold, consumed. 
In the event of any disturbance, uprising or riot, or any other emergency endangering life, property or public safety, it shall be the duty of the chief of police to promptly close any and all places in the city where intoxicating alcoholic beverages are sold, consumed or otherwise dispensed, and to require such places to remain closed for the period of such emergency. 
Cross reference— Civil emergency curfew, § 22-100 et seq.  
Sec. 4-9. - Sale to certain persons prohibited. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to sell, give or furnish in any manner any alcoholic beverage at any time or place to any person who is known to be insane or mentally incapacitated, or to any person who is visibly intoxicated, or to any person who is known to habitually drink alcoholic beverages to excess, or to any person who is known to be a habitual user of narcotics or other habit-forming drugs, or to knowingly sell, furnish or give the same to any person for delivery to such person. 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 10265-32.  
Sec. 4-10. - Sale to minors. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to sell, give or furnish in any manner any intoxicating alcoholic beverage at any time or place to any person under 21 years of age, or to knowingly sell, furnish or give the same to any person for delivery to such minors. 
State Law reference— Similar state law, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 10265-31.  
Sec. 4-11. - Purchase, possession by minors. 
It shall be unlawful for any person under the age of 21 years to purchase, consume or have in his or her possession on any public street or in any public place any intoxicating alcoholic beverage. 
State Law reference— Similar state law, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 10265-31.  
Sec. 4-12. - False representation of age by minor. 
It shall be unlawful for any person under the age of 21 years to make a false statement relative to his age for the purpose of obtaining alcoholic beverages. 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 10265-31.  
Sec. 4-13. - Employment of minors. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to employ in any capacity in connection with the sale or dispensing of alcoholic beverages in a package store or otherwise, any person under the age of 21 years.  
Sec. 4-14. - Possession, consumption in public places. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to have in his possession or to consume intoxicating alcoholic beverages as defined by any statute of this state in the municipal school buildings, stadiums, any public playgrounds or public parks, or any fire station, or on any other public grounds, buildings, parks or other places owned, maintained and operated by the city, except upon prior approval by the mayor and board of aldermen of the city. 
(Ord. of 6-5-90)  
Sec. 4-15. - Consumption on public streets, sidewalks. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to consume any intoxicating alcoholic beverage while on a public street or sidewalk of the city. 
Cross reference— Streets and sidewalks, Ch. 29.  
Sec. 4-16. - Drunkenness. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to appear in any public place or on any public street in a drunken condition, and it shall be the duty of the police officers of the city to immediately remove and jail any such person. 
State Law reference— Intoxication as an offense, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 2291.  
Secs. 4-17—4-26. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - BEER AND WINE[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Authority, regulations regarding local option for sale, distribution of beer and light wine, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, §§ 10208, 10208.5; municipal authority to regulate sale, § 10224; license tax, § 10240; municipal authority to levy privilege tax, limit on same, § 10263; regulations as to wine and beer, § 10207 et seq. 
 
Sec. 4-27. - License required. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in the business of the retail sale of beer and wine as permitted under Section 10207, Mississippi Code Annotated, 1942, without having first applied for and obtained from the city a privilege license to engage in such business.  
Sec. 4-28. - Payment of tax; application for license. 
Any person desiring to engage in the retail sale of beer and wine shall pay the city a license tax at the same rate as that imposed by Sections 10240 and 10263, Mississippi Code Annotated, 1942, as amended, for the privilege of engaging in such business, and shall file with the city clerk a written application setting forth the following: 
(a)  The name of the applicant. 
(b)  An affidavit affirmatively showing the applicant above the age of 21 years; a person of good moral character; a citizen of the United States and the state; that the applicant has not been convicted of a felony within ten years preceding the date of his application; nor convicted within five years preceding the date of his application, of any laws of this or other states, or of the United States, relating to alcoholic liquors or gambling. 
(c)  If the applicant is a copartnership, all members of the copartnership must be named and shall be qualified to obtain the license. 
(d)  If applicant is a corporation, the names of all officers and directors thereof and any stockholder owning more than five percent of the stock of such corporation, all requirements must be met by such persons, except requirements as to residence of officers, directors and stockholders, which shall not apply.  
Sec. 4-29. - Notice of application. 
No license shall be issued under this article until the expiration of seven calendar days from the publication of notice as herein provided. Said notice shall be placed by the applicant, at applicant's cost, in a newspaper published in the city and having general circulation therein. Such notice shall be published one time, and state essentially the following: 
"I,    (Name of Applicant)    , have made application to the City of Canton, Mississippi, for a privilege license to engage in the retail sale of beer and wine, as permitted by law at    (Street Address)    in the City of Canton, Mississippi."  
Sec. 4-30. - Hearing upon objection to application. 
If, in the event written objection is received by the city clerk prior to the expiration of the seven day period stated in section 4-4, which is made by a person owning land or real property, or having business interests operating within a radius of 160 feet of the applicant's proposed retail outlet, then no license shall be issued unless authorized by the mayor and board of aldermen. 
As soon as possible after filing of such objection, but no later than 21 days from such filing, a hearing shall be held by the mayor and aldermen. At such hearing the objector shall have the burden of showing that the granting of such license shall be contrary to the public health, morals and safety. Provided, however, that said license shall be issued unless the mayor and board of aldermen affirmatively find that the operation of said retail outlet would adversely affect the public health, morals and safety, giving reasonable consideration to the effect of said retail outlet on property values and business within said 160-foot radius, and the location of schools, churches, and other such institutions within the immediate area. Provided, however, no said retail outlet shall be deemed to have an effect on any such school, church, or other institution if more than 800 feet away from same.  
Sec. 4-31. - Application to present licensees. 
Notwithstanding any provision in this article to the contrary, any holder of a privilege license from the city to engage in the business of the retail sale of wine and beer, shall not be required to file said written application as provided for under this article, so long as such present holder renews his license at the same location or retail outlet. Rights of the present holder granted under this section shall not be transferable.  
Sec. 4-32. - Revocation or suspension of license. 
Beer licenses must be revoked or suspended for the following causes: 
(1)  Willful failure or refusal by any licensee to comply with any of the provisions of Mississippi law or of any rule or regulation adopted by the city in regard to the sale or consumption of alcoholic beverages, beer and/or wine. 
(2)  The making of any materially false statement in any application for a license. 
(3)  Two or more convictions of one or more of the clerks, agents or employees of the licensee, of any violation of Mississippi law or municipal ordinance upon the premises covered by such license within a period of two years. 
(4)  The possession on the premises of any retail license of any alcoholic beverages, beer or wine upon which the tax has not been paid. 
(5)  The willful failure of any licensee to keep the records or make the reports required by Mississippi law, or to allow an inspection of such records or premises by any duly authorized person. 
(6)  The suspension or revocation of a license issued to the licensee by the state or federal government, or conviction of violating any federal law relating to alcoholic beverages; 
(7)  The conducting of any form of gambling on the premises of any licensee or on any premises connected therewith or the presence on any such premises of any gambling device with the knowledge of the licensee. 
(Ord. of 5-3-84, § 1)  
Sec. 4-33. - Possession of unsealed containers. 
It shall be unlawful for any party to have in his or her possession or to carry, handle or transport beer on any parking lot or on any public street, sidewalk or way within the city except in sealed containers which have not been opened, punctured or otherwise handled or treated so as to make it possible to extract the contents of such container since the beer was originally placed in such container, except for an event for which a temporary waiver has been obtained by the governing authorities. Provided, nothing shall be construed as prohibiting the possession of beer inside vehicles parked on private lots of business licensed to sell beer in the municipality. 
(Ord. of 6-7-14)  
Sec. 4-34. - Selling to insane or intoxicated persons, drunkards, etc. 
It shall be unlawful for any permittee holding a retailer's beer permit or other person to sell or furnish beer or wine to any person who is known to be insane or mentally defective, or to any person who is visibly intoxicated, or to any person who is known to habitually drink alcoholic beverages to excess, or to any person who is known to be a habitual user of narcotics or other habit-forming drugs. 
(Ord. of 5-3-83, § 1)  
Sec. 4-35. - Special licensing of certain establishments for on-premises consumption. 
Whereas, there exists a substantial number of establishments in the city which provide amusement, sale of beer and allow consumption thereof on its premises; and, 
Whereas, the present ordinances of the city do not specifically deal with such establishments and that it would be in the best interests of the city and its citizens to regulate and license such businesses further in the interest of health, peace and welfare of the city and its citizens. 
Be it ordained by the mayor and board of aldermen as follows, to wit: 
(a)  License. It shall be unlawful for any person, corporation or partnership to engage in the business of retail sale of beer as permitted under Section 67-3-1, et seq., Mississippi Code Annotated of 1972, wherein the consumption of beer or any other alcoholic beverages allowed on the premises of such business, without having first applied for and obtained from the city a specific license in compliance herewith. 
(b)  Written application. Any person, corporation, or partnership desiring such license shall file with the city clerk a written application as required by section 4-28. 
(c)  Approval of certain officials. Such person, corporation, or partnership shall attach to the above required application written approval of the Madison County Health Department, fire chief of the city, building inspector of the city, Canton municipal utility inspector, and police chief of the city as to the persons, site and premises meeting any and all applicable provisions of state, federal and local statutes, resolutions, orders or ordinances. 
(d)  Fee; renewal. Such person, corporation or partnership shall present with such application required herein the amount of $50.00 and for the calendar year for which the license shall be issued, such person, corporation or partnership shall renew such license by following the above outlined procedure in making such payment on or before the tenth day of January of each succeeding year after the issuance of the original license. Any such premises subject to this section shall comply herewith on or before 60 days from the effective date of this section which shall be 30 days from the date of passage. 
(e)  Relationship of section to other legislation. The terms and conditions of this section shall be supplementary to any and all existing ordinances in this regard and that this ordinance shall not supersede, modify or revoke any requirements heretofore set out in section 4-27. 
(f)  Nontransferable. Any license granted hereunder shall not be transferable. 
(g)  Penalty. Any person, partnership or corporation violating any of the provisions of this section shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and on conviction thereof shall be fined not more than $500.00 or imprisoned not to exceed six months or by both such fine and imprisonment and that the operation of a business and/or premises without the license required herein shall constitute a separate offense for each day of operation. 
(h)  Severability. Should any provision of this section be declared unconstitutional or void by a court of competent jurisdiction, the other provisions hereof shall remain in full force and effect. 
(i)  Appeal. Any person, partnership or corporation aggrieved by the enforcement, implementation or response of parties named in this section and required for its enforcement may appeal and ask for a review and reversal of any action taken as required herein to and from the mayor and board of aldermen in a special or regular meeting. 
(j)  Closing time of business. Any person, partnership or corporation subject to the terms and conditions of this section shall close its place of business to the public at or before 1:00 a.m. each day and shall not allow activity therein until sunrise of the same day. 
(Ord. of 2-19-80, §§ 1—10) 
Editor's note— Ord. of Feb. 19, 1980, §§ 1—10, did not specifically amend the Code; hence, codification as § 4-35 has been at the editor's discretion. The "whereas" clauses have been included for purposes of clarity. 
Cross reference— Amusements, Ch. 5.  
Sec. 4-36. - Sunday sales of beer prohibited. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful to give to be consumed or to sell beer between the hours of 12:00 midnight and 4:00 p.m. on Sunday for on-premises consumption within the corporate limits of the city. 
(b)  Each violation of the above prohibition shall constitute a separate misdemeanor and shall be punishable by a fine of not more than $500.00 or imprisonment for not more than six months, or both, at the discretion of the court. 
(Ord. of 1-18-83, §§ 1, 2) 
Editor's note— At the editor's discretion, §§ 1 and 2 of an ordinance adopted Jan. 18, 1983, have been included as § 4-36. 
Cross reference— Sunday food sales in certain establishments prohibited, § 22-7.  
Sec. 4-37. - Premises located within fire zone. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any restaurant, cafe or other retail establishment located within the fire zone within the city, to have any sign, lighted or otherwise, or printing on the outside of the premises covered by his permit or license, advertising, announcing or advising of the sale of beer on said premises. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful to keep, store or display any beer price list or promotional matter in the windows, doors or other openings of any premises within the fire zone wherein beer shall be sold for on-premises consumption. 
(Ord. of 5-3-83, §§ 2, 3) 
Editor's note— At the editor's discretion, §§ 2 and 3 of an ordinance adopted May 3, 1983, have been included herein as § 4-37.  
Sec. 4-38. - Visibility of interior from outside premises. 
It shall be unlawful for any restaurant, cafe or other retail establishment with an on-premises beer permit to leave open or in an open position any doors, openings and/or windows which would, if permitted to remain open, allow passersby to see in or inside the premises. 
(Ord. of 5-3-83, § 4) 
Editor's note— At the editor's discretion, § 4 of an ordinance adopted May 3, 1983, has been included herein as § 4-38.  
Chapter 5 - AMUSEMENTS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Special license required for on-premise consumption of beer at certain places, § 4-35; certain amusements prohibited in city parks, § 23-1. 
State Law reference— Authority to regulate circuses, carnivals and fairs, etc., Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 3374-131. 
 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Sec. 5-1. - Permit required for carnivals, circuses, shows, etc. 
No traveling or itinerant street carnival, circus, show, theater, tent show or theatrical exhibition or show or exhibition of any other kind or type shall show or exhibit within the city until first securing a permit from the city clerk and mayor, and until all privilege and other taxes due by law are paid to the tax collector.  
Sec. 5-2. - Bond or liability insurance required for amusement rides. 
No person shall conduct, operate, manage or sponsor any ferris wheel, merry-go-round or other amusement ride operated for hire or for the purpose of promoting or advertising any trade or business, without first filing with the city clerk a bond or certificate of liability insurance, in the amount of at least $50,000.00, indemnifying the public against damages sustained by reason of the operation of such ride. Such bond or certificate of insurance shall be subject to approval by the city attorney. This section shall apply to all persons, whether or not a license or permit is required by any other provision of this Code, state law or city ordinance, rule or regulation.  
Secs. 5-3—5-17. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - POOLROOMS, BILLIARD HALLS[2] 
Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— General licensing regulations, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 9696-28; authority of city to regulate, § 3374-131. 
 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
 
Secs. 5-18—5-27. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 2. - LICENSE[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
Cross reference— Local privilege taxes, § 18-16 et seq. 
 
Sec. 5-28. - Application. 
Before any license shall be issued to any person to operate a poolroom or billiard room, such person shall make an application to the city tax collector which shall be filed in the office of the city clerk and shall be in the following form: 
To the Tax Collector of the City of Canton, Mississippi: 
I (or we) hereby make application for a privilege license to operate _______ pool or billiard tables in a room at _______, Canton, Mississippi. 
I state on oath that I (or we) will not knowingly permit any betting on any game played therein, or drinking of any alcoholic beverages or alcoholic mixture therein or on the premises adjacent thereto. 
Signed: _____ 
Sworn to before me this _______ day of _______, 19___. 
_____
Notary Public 
State Law reference— Similar state law, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 9696-29.  
Sec. 5-29. - Affidavit bond required. 
Before any pool or billiard room license may be issued, the applicant shall be required to make and file in the office of the city clerk, in addition to the application therefor, the following affidavit: 
STATE OF MISSISSIPPI 
COUNTY OF MADISON 
CITY OF CANTON 
TO THE MAYOR AND BOARD OF ALDERMEN OF THE CITY OF CANTON, COUNTY OF MADISON, MISSISSIPPI: 
I, having made application for privilege tax license to operate a poolroom or billiard room or tables in or at the following place, to wit: 
In the City of Canton, Mississippi, I hereby state, under oath that I have never been convicted of violating the prohibition laws of the State of Mississippi; further that I will operate said business in compliance with all ordinances of the City of Canton, Mississippi; further in the event I should knowingly violate any section or sections of any ordinance of the City of Canton, Mississippi, pertaining to the operation of poolrooms or billiard rooms, the said city shall have the right to immediately close the doors of and terminate my said business and declare forfeited the bond herewith deposited for the faithful performance and observance of the ordinances of the City of Canton, Mississippi, and the statutes of the State of Mississippi, with reference to the operation of a poolroom; I will not permit any alcoholic drinks to be sold on said premises, nor will I permit any drinking of alcoholic beverages on said premises. I will not permit any gambling on said premises; nor will I permit any person under the age of 21 years to frequent or patronize the same. 
Signed: _____ 
STATE OF MISSISSIPPI 
COUNTY OF MADISON 
Personally appeared before me, the undersigned authority, _______, Notary Public, in and for said County and State, who acknowledged that he signed the above and foregoing application and that he will abide by and comply with all obligations imposed on him therein. 
Given under my hand and seal of office this the _______ day of _______, 19___. 
_____
NOTARY PUBLIC 
CANTON, MADISON COUNTY, 
MISSISSIPPI.  
Sec. 5-30. - Conditions of issuance, denial. 
The city shall not issue any pool or billiard room license to any person who has been convicted of violating any of the prohibition laws of the state. Before the city shall issue said license, the applicant shall file with the city clerk the application and affidavit, which shall remain on file ten days for consideration by the mayor and board of aldermen. If the mayor and board of aldermen in their discretion decide that it would not be for the best interest of or promote the general welfare of the city or its citizens or shall not be expedient, for said license to be issued to said person making application therefor, they shall so notify the city clerk and said license shall not be issued. The mayor and board of aldermen may refuse, in their discretion, any such application.  
Sec. 5-31. - Revocation; closure of business. 
If at any time the mayor and board of aldermen shall ascertain and adjudge that any business is not being operated in accordance with all applicable provisions of this Code, city ordinances or state laws, or that it will not be expedient or for the best interest of and will promote good morals or general welfare of the city for the operation of such pool or billiard room to continue, or for any reason satisfactory to the mayor and board of aldermen, then they shall have the right to immediately order said business closed, and the license therefor cancelled, revoked and surrendered. On failure or refusal of the licensee to close his business when ordered to do so, the bond that he has given therefor shall be immediately forfeited; and if such person fails to close promptly such poolroom or billiard room, then the mayor is hereby authorized to close the same immediately.  
Secs. 5-32—5-50. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE III. - BINGO GAMES[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
Editor's note— An ordinance of January 2, 1990, did not specifically amend the Code; therefore, inclusion of §§ 1—11 as Art. III, §§ 5-51—5-61 was at the discretion of the editor. 
 
Sec. 5-51. - To be held by certain nonprofit organizations only.
