Bingo games as defined in section 97-33-49 Mississippi Code of 1972, Annotated, and as amended, are permitted only when held by and for the benefit of any nonprofit civic, educational, wildlife conservation or religious organization with all proceeds going to said organization. 
(Ord. of 1-2-90, § 1)  
Sec. 5-52. - Definitions. 
As used in this article, the following terms have the following meanings ascribed to them unless the context clearly indicates otherwise: 
(1)  Person means an individual, corporation, association, partnership or other entity. 
(2)  Nonprofit civic, educational, wildlife conservation and religious organizations shall mean only those persons or organizations recognized as such by the State of Mississippi and/or the Internal Revenue Service under Internal Revenue Service Code of 1954, as amended, Section 501(C)(3) (4) (7) (8) (10) (19). No person may conduct a bingo game under this article by virtue of a temporary association with such a nonprofit civic, educational, wildlife conservation and religious organization. 
(Ord. of 1-2-90, § 2)  
Sec. 5-53. - Application for permit; fee. 
All applicants for a bingo permit shall be required to appear before the mayor and board of aldermen of the City of Canton to apply for such permit and such application must include the following: 
(1)  The name and permanent address of the person making the application. 
(2)  The name and permanent address of the registered agent of the applicant. The registered agent must be a resident of Madison County, Mississippi, and shall be the agent on whom any process, notice or demand required or permitted by law to be served on the licensee may be served. The registered agent must agree in writing to act as agent and a copy of that agreement shall be filed with the application. If the registered agent cannot be found at the stated address or if the licensee fails to maintain a registered agent, the permit of the applicant shall be considered revoked immediately until such time as an agent is found or named. Further, the city clerk is the agent of the licensee only for the purpose of service of process, demand or notice. Service on the city clerk is made by delivering duplicate copies of such process, notice or demand to her office, she shall immediately forward one copy of such process, notice or demand to the permanent address of the registered agent by certified or registered mail. This section does not limit or otherwise affect the right of any person to serve a process, notice or demand in any other manner authorized by law. 
(3)  Proof must be shown that the applicant has acquired all other city, county, state and federal permits and licenses to include an Internal Revenue Service exemption letter dated within six months of the date of application. 
(4)  If the applicant is an association or a corporation, the applicant must also include the names and addresses of the members of the association or the officers of the corporation. The applicant must state the date of incorporation and the state in which it was incorporated. If the corporation is a corporation under the laws of another state, the applicant must state the date on which the corporation qualified to do business as a foreign corporation in this state. Also the applicant shall furnish the following: 
a.  A detailed statement of charitable contributions for the last five years; 
b.  List of persons responsible for distribution of contributions for the past five years; 
c.  List of officers for the past five years; 
d.  List of current members in good standing and length of time in good standing, including names and street addresses and date each member joined the organization; 
e.  Board of directors' minutes for the past five years; and 
f.  A copy of the corporate or organization bylaws. 
(5)  The frequency, hours and days of proposed operation of the bingo game. 
(6)  The maximum number of players that may be accommodated at any such bingo game. 
a.  This shall include the size of the building and the area used for the conduct of bingo games in square feet. 
b.  A detailed description of the concession facilities. 
c.  Rent paid on the building if applicable. If rent is paid for the use of the building, the applicant shall include the name and address of the rentor, if the rentor is an association or a corporation, the applicant must also include the names and addresses of the members of the association or the officers of the corporation. The applicant must state the date of incorporation and the state in which rentor incorporated. If the rentor corporation is a corporation under the laws of another state, the applicant must state the date on which the corporation qualified to do business as a foreign corporation in this state. 
(7)  A detailed statement shall be provided of the intended use of funds raised for charitable, religious or educational purposes and the intended payee(s). 
(8)  Permits for bingo games shall initially be effective from the date of issuance for a period not to exceed one year. An applicant may reapply before the expiration of such license for an additional period of licensure not to exceed two years. This may be granted and renewed biannually pursuant to and in accordance with the procedures and standards which governed their grant. In the event that a license is revoked before the expiration for any reason, it may be reinstated for the remainder of its original term after application to and approval of the mayor and board of aldermen. 
(9)  Application for permit: 
a.  Each permit application shall be accompanied by a nonrefundable $500.00 fee. 
b.  Each application for renewal shall be accompanied by a nonrefundable $500.00 fee. 
c.  Each application for license reinstatement shall be accompanied by a nonrefundable $500.00 fee. 
d.  Each licensee shall, prior to conducting a bingo game, furnish to the City of Canton, a good and sufficient penal bond in the amount of $2,000.00 conditioned that if such licensee shall comply with all provisions relating to this article said obligation shall be void, otherwise to remain in full force and effect. 
(Ord. of 1-2-90, § 3)  
Sec. 5-54. - Quarterly and annual reports; record. 
All persons authorized by the City of Canton to operate bingo establishments are hereby required to file quarterly and annual reports of receipts and disbursements. These reports shall be filed with the city clerk on the forms prescribed by that office. These reports are due on dates prescribed by the city clerk. 
The person to whom a permit for bingo games is issued shall maintain an itemized record of income, expenditures and disbursements, including the date and the name of any person to whom disbursements of profits are made, in connection with such games. Such record shall be in a bound book which shall be located on the premises where the bingo games are held and which shall be available for inspection or reproduction at reasonable hours by the city clerk or the designated representative of that office. 
(Ord. of 1-2-90, § 4)  
Sec. 5-55. - Regulations—Generally. 
(a)  Bingo may be conducted by an organization on not more than one day a week. 
(b)  No person may conduct bingo on behalf of an organization who: 
(1)  Has been convicted of, or has pled guilty to or nolo contendere to, any felony or offense involving gambling or moral turpitude, violations of any state bingo ordinance, or has participated in a statutory diversion program for any felony or any offense involving gambling or moral turpitude or violations of any state bingo ordinance. 
(2)  Has not been a member in good standing for not less than one year, prior to the date of application of the bingo permit, of the organization applying for such permit. 
(3)  Has not been a legal resident of this state and county for not less than one year. 
(c)  No member of an organization authorized to conduct bingo games shall receive compensation, including but not limited to tips, for conducting or assisting in the conduct of bingo. No member of an organization which has a permit to conduct bingo games shall participate in any game of bingo within this county. 
(d)  A licensee may reasonably compensate for security and janitorial services rendered to the organization in connection with the conduct of bingo. The licensee shall report on a quarterly basis to the city clerk on such forms as that office may prescribe listing the following: 
(1)  Names, addresses, and either social security numbers or employer's identification numbers (as applicable) of those receiving such compensation. 
(2)  Date(s) when such services were rendered and person hours involved. 
(3)  Date and amount paid to those rendering the services. 
(e)  A licensee may purchase supplies necessary for the conduct of bingo. The licensee shall report to the city clerk on such forms as prescribed by that office the following: 
(1)  Date and amount of purchase. 
(2)  Name and address of supplier. 
(3)  Description of items or services purchased. 
(f)  The serial numbers of all bingo cards purchased shall be reported. It shall be unlawful, and grounds for revocation of license, to have on the premises where a bingo game is conducted bingo cards without a serial number and such serial number and date of purchase not recorded on the appropriate form supplied by the city clerk. 
(Ord. of 1-2-90, § 5)  
Sec. 5-56. - Same—Advertising; age limitations; conduct of games. 
(a)  Advertising for bingo shall be limited to: 
(1)  A ground-mounted sign not to exceed 35 square feet. 
(2)  No more than one paid advertisement monthly in a local newspaper shall be allowed, and such advertisement shall not exceed three inches by two columns. 
(3)  The organization's own newsletter, provided that this newsletter may not be disseminated to the public but only to bona fide members of the organization when it contains bingo news or advertising. 
(4)  All advertising must contain the correct name of the licensee in type no smaller than the largest type otherwise in the advertisement. 
(5)  The use of a trade name by the licensee is prohibited. 
(b)  No person under 18 years of age, whether a paying player or volunteer worker shall be allowed on the premises during any bingo game or for one hour before or after such bingo game. 
(c)  No more than one organization shall be permitted to conduct a bingo game at a location. 
(d)  No member of an authorized organization may directly or indirectly have any interest in any building where bingo is conducted, including but not limited to, owner, lessee, operator, manager, concessioners or employee. 
(e)  No person shall be allowed to conduct bingo, within this municipality, for more than one organization at any time, and if a person stops conducting bingo for a particular organization, he is prohibited from conducting bingo for any other organization for a period of one year. 
(Ord. of 1-2-90, § 6)  
Sec. 5-57. - Same—Use of revenue; cards and materials. 
(a)  Not less than 50 percent of gross revenues shall be used for religious, charitable, or educational purposes. These religious, charitable, or educational purposes shall not in any manner include repair or maintenance of the building or property wherein the bingo game is conducted or any immediately adjacent properties. These religious, charitable, or educational purposes shall also not include purchase, debt retirement, leasing or any improvement of the property on which the bingo game is conducted or any immediately adjacent property. Any income received from the investment of bingo revenues shall be used for religious, charitable, or educational purposes in addition to the 50 percent. The proceeds used for religious, charitable, or educational purposes shall be disbursed as payment for goods or services provided by the payee to the appropriate religious, charitable, or educational beneficiary for which the bingo was conducted, and such payee designated by the licensee as payee on the application. 
(b)  Bingo cards: 
(1)  Each card or package of cards shall have the price of that card or package of cards printed on the face of the card or package. 
(2)  Each card or package shall be sold at the price printed thereon without any discount for any reason. 
(3)  A bingo card package shall not be disassembled and sold as individual cards. 
(4)  No card or package of cards may be awarded as a prize. 
(5)  No licensee shall permit any person to play on a free card. 
(6)  Each bingo card shall have printed on the face a serial number. 
(c)  No licensee shall discard or destroy any bingo materials or supplies unless the licensee discards or destroys such materials in the presence of and with the written permission of the city clerk or his designated representative. The licensee shall deliver to the city clerk, prior to this discarding or destruction, a written record including the quantity and serial number of such materials and supplies. 
(Ord. of 1-2-90, § 7)  
Sec. 5-58. - Same—Prize amounts; proceeds from games; disbursement of funds. 
(a)  Prize amounts shall not exceed 50 percent of gross revenues. 
(b)  Proceeds from bingo shall be kept in a separate special bingo account which shall be in the form of a checking account in a bank with a branch in Madison County, Mississippi. Such checking account shall have preprinted consecutively numbered checks, and all checks shall be payable to a specific person or corporation. At no time shall any check be made payable to cash. All checks (voided and otherwise) shall be retained and accounted for as part of the quarterly records required of the licensee. All checks must require two signatures. No person may borrow or use any bingo funds as a personal loan of any kind whatsoever. All gross receipts from each bingo game shall be deposited in the special bingo game account no later than the next business day following the date of the bingo game. Withdrawals from this account may be made for only the following purposes: 
(1)  Payment of prizes; 
(2)  Payment of authorized expenses; 
(3)  Disbursement of net proceeds for a religious, charitable, or educational purpose; and 
(4)  Transfer to one interest-bearing account pending disbursement. Any transfer from such interest-bearing account shall only be to the special bingo account established by this section. 
(c)  The disbursement of funds from an organization's bingo account shall only be by check. There shall be no commingling of any funds of the licensee with the bingo funds and any such funds commingled shall be considered to be bingo funds and governed by the applicable sections of this article. 
(1)  A licensee shall award all prizes by check only. 
(2)  Neither the licensee nor any worker, member or any other person connected with the organization may cash a prize check. It shall be prohibited for the licensee to in any way provide check-cashing services or to allow such services on the premises where the bingo game is conducted for a period of two hours before and after such bingo game is conducted. 
(d)  (1)  The licensee shall maintain a prize register to include at least the following information: 
(i)  Name of licensee. 
(ii)  Date of bingo event. 
(iii)  Amount of prize. 
(iv)  Name, addresses, telephone number, driver's license number, if any, and signature of the winner. 
(v)  Social Security number of winner. 
(2)  Failure of a prize winner to provide the information required disqualifies a person from receiving a prize. 
(3)  The maximum prize for any one bingo game shall be $500.00 cash and the maximum total amount of prizes awarded on any one date at a bingo game shall not exceed $3,000.00. 
(e)  The licensee shall maintain its bingo records on a cash accounting basis. The licensee shall maintain its records, including the daily prize register so that an audit may be conducted in accordance with generally accepted accounting principals. 
(1)  The licensee shall retain its records for inspection by the city clerk or her designee for five years from the end of the licensee's fiscal year. 
(2)  The licensee shall on a quarterly basis account to the city clerk on forms prescribed by that office. These reports shall contain quarterly and year-to-date financial information and shall be filed within 30 days of the end of each quarter. Such reports shall be made on forms approved by the city clerk. 
(Ord. of 1-2-90, § 8)  
Sec. 5-59. - Additional regulations concerning the conduct of games. 
The following are additional regulations governing the conduct of bingo games: 
(1)  No alcoholic beverages may be served or consumed at a location at which bingo games are conducted for a period of six hours before or after such an event. 
(2)  No player, worker, security guard or any other person at a bingo game may be in possession of a firearm, knife, club, or other dangerous weapon during such time as a bingo game is in progress. 
(3)  Violation of any section of this article shall be grounds for revocation of licensee's bingo permit. 
(4)  Conduct of bingo is subject to all other applicable ordinances of the City of Canton. 
(5)  Bingo games shall not be conducted except between the hours of 6 p.m. and 11 p.m. 
(Ord. of 1-2-90, § 9)  
Sec. 5-60. - Exemptions; violations. 
Nonprofit civic, educational, wildlife conservation and religious organizations meeting all of the requirements of this section are exempt from all but section 5-58(d)(1)(i—v), (2) of this article provided: 
(1)  Those organizations have or hold bingo games less than four times in any calendar year and always more than one month apart; 
(2)  Those organizations award as prizes only merchandise and/or gift certificates which cannot be converted to cash; 
(3)  The maximum prize value for any one bingo game shall not exceed $1,000.00, and the maximum value of the prizes at any bingo event shall not exceed $5,000.00; 
(4)  The information required in section 5-58(d)(1)(i—v) shall be reported to the office of the city clerk on forms approved by that office within ten days of the bingo event; and 
(5)  Any person, firm or corporation who shall knowingly and willfully violate the terms, conditions, or provisions of this article shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof shall be sentenced to pay a fine not to exceed $500.00 and/or six months imprisonment or both. In the case of continuing violations without reasonable effort on the part of the defendant to correct the same, each day the violation continues thereafter shall be a separate offense. 
(Ord. of 1-2-90, § 10)  
Sec. 5-61. - Adherence to regulations. 
All organizations conducting bingo games under permits or licenses granted by any governing body other than the City of Canton are hereby given 90 days from the effective date of this article to adhere to the requirements of this article or cease conducting bingo games in this municipality. 
(Ord. of 1-2-90, § 11)  
Sec. 5-62. - Games to be held pursuant to charitable bingo law. 
(a)  All bingo games shall be held pursuant to the charitable bingo law of the state. 
(b)  No alcoholic beverages may be served or consumed at a location at which bingo games are conducted pursuant to the charitable bingo law. 
(c)  No bingo games as defined by the charitable bingo law of the state, except those bingo games conducted by churches and schools, may be conducted within 1,000 feet of a church, school or residence. 
(Ord. of 3-2-93, §§ 1—3) 
Editor's note— An ordinance adopted March 2, 1993, §§ 1—3, did not specifically amend the Code; therefore, inclusion as § 5-62 was at the discretion of the editor.  
Chapter 6 - ANIMALS AND FOWL[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Noisy animals, fowl prohibited, § 21-7; health and sanitation, Ch. 15. 
State Law reference— General stock law, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, §§ 4864, 4870 et seq.; general provisions regarding cruelty to animals, §§ 2067—2075. 
 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Sec. 6-1. - Stock running at large. 
If any person shall knowingly, wilfully or negligently allow any horse, mule, jack, jennett, stallion, bull, ox, cow, calf, hog, sheep or goat, in his possession or custody, to run at large upon the streets of the city, or unlawfully on the premises of another, within the corporate limits he shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1930, § 201)  
Secs. 6-2—6-16. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - IMPOUNDMENT OF LIVESTOCK 
 
Sec. 6-17. - Authorized. 
Every animal which shall be found in violation of the provisions of this chapter in or upon the streets, alleys, sidewalks or footways of this city shall be promptly captured and impounded by the police officers of the city. 
(Code 1930, § 150)  
Sec. 6-18. - Notice to owner—Issuance. 
Any animal impounded under this article shall be kept, fed and watered while in the pound, and immediately upon the impounding of any such animal the poundmaster shall notify the owner or agent thereof, in the following manner, viz: 
(a)  If the owner or his agent reside in this city, and be known to the poundmaster, he or some other member of his family shall have personal notice, oral or written. 
(b)  If the owner or agent be known to the poundmaster, but be a nonresident of this city, notice in writing or printing shall be sent by mail or private conveyance to such owner or agent. 
(c)  If the owner be unknown, notice shall be given by written or printed notices posted at the courthouse, post office and city hall. 
(Code 1930, § 152)  
Sec. 6-19. - Same—Contents. 
The notice provided for by this article shall contain a description of the animal impounded under this article by color, sex, ear mark, probable age, and if cows, whether milch or dry cows, together with the date of impounding. 
(Code 1930, § 153)  
Sec. 6-20. - Redemption. 
For the release of any animal impounded under the provisions of this article, the poundmaster shall demand and be entitled to receive from the owner, agent or person claiming the possession or control thereof, the fees and emoluments hereinafter designated, and on payment of such charges, the animal so impounded shall be released to the person claiming same. 
If, after three days' notice of the impoundment of an animal under this article such animal shall remain in the pound, the poundmaster shall advertise and sell the same, between 11:00 a.m. and 4:00 p.m., to the highest bidder for cash, in front of the south door of the courthouse, after giving three days' notice of the time, place and terms of sale, including a description of the animal to be sold, as prescribed in above section, by posting written or printed notices thereof in three public places, viz: One at the courthouse, one at the post office, and one at the mayor's office; provided, every sale under this section shall be made subject to the owner's right of redemption within 60 days. 
(Code 1930, §§ 151, 154)  
Sec. 6-21. - Disposition of sale proceeds. 
All money received by the poundmaster for the sale of impounded animals shall, after deducting his fees, be immediately paid into the city depository to the credit of the general fund. The poundmaster shall make a special report of said sale to the council at the next meeting, describing the animal or animals sold, the amount bid and paid therefor, the itemized amount of his fees deducted, and the amount paid into the city depository. 
(Code 1930, § 155)  
Sec. 6-22. - Owner may redeem after sale. 
The owner of any animal impounded under this article and sold shall have the right to redeem the same within 60 days after said sale, by paying to the city clerk, for the benefit of the purchaser, the amount of the legal fees of the poundmaster for which said animal was sold, and $0.10 for each day subsequent to the day of said sale, together with 25 percentum on the amount paid for such animal by the purchaser, as damages for the purchaser; whereupon it shall be the duty of the clerk to immediately pay said sum into the city depository to the credit of the general fund, and to give the owner a written order on the purchaser for said animal. It shall be the duty of the purchaser to deliver to the owner the animal, in compliance with said order; and for failure so to do the purchaser shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1930, § 156)  
Sec. 6-23. - Use of animal restricted. 
It shall be unlawful for any person buying any animal at a pound sale to kill, sell, remove from the county, or otherwise dispose of such animal for 60 days subsequent to said sale; but shall hold the same during said time, subject to redemption under the provisions of this article. 
(Code 1930, § 159)  
Sec. 6-24. - Allowance for use of stock. 
If the purchaser of any stock sold by the poundmaster shall use same within the 60 days allowed for its redemption, then his claim for damages and charges shall be offset by whatever is the reasonable worth of the use of such animal or animals. 
(Code 1930, § 162)  
Secs. 6-25—6-34. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE III. - BIRD SANCTUARY[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Bird sanctuary, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 5835 et seq.; unprotected birds, §§ 5838, 5868. 
 
Sec. 6-35. - Designation. 
The entire area embraced within the corporate limits of the city is hereby designated as a bird sanctuary. 
(Ord. of 12-6-56)  
Sec. 6-36. - Mistreatment restricted. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to trap, hunt, shoot, or attempt to shoot, or molest in any manner any bird, or to rob bird nests; providing, it shall be lawful to destroy starlings or similar birds (such as jays, or English sparrows), or fowls when such birds or fowls are found to be congregating in such numbers in a particular locality that they constitute a nuisance or menace to health or property. 
(Ord. of 12-6-56)  
Sec. 6-37. - Action by city. 
If any birds are declared by qualified authorities to be creating a public nuisance, and the mayor and board of aldermen be so informed, appropriate action may be taken by duly constituted officials after a thorough investigation. 
(Ord. of 12-6-56)  
Sec. 6-38. - Trapping, killing. 
Trapping or killing of birds which have been designated as a public nuisance shall not be resorted to unless Audubon Societies, bird clubs, garden clubs, or humane societies are unable to find a satisfactory alternative within a reasonable time. 
(Ord. of 12-6-56)  
Secs. 6-39—6-48. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE IV. - DOGS[3] 
Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
Cross reference— Mistreatment of police dogs, § 27-1. 
State Law reference— Dogs generally, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 6815 et seq. 
 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
 
Sec. 6-49. - Vaccination, tag. 
It shall be the duty of the owner of every dog within the city, six months of age or over, to have such dog vaccinated against rabies annually with an approved dosage of an approved anti-rabic vaccine properly administered by one legally authorized to administer the same and to see that such dog when so vaccinated wears about its neck and securely bradded to the collar a metal tag approved by the state board of health with the serial number of the vaccination and the year in which the dog was inoculated stamped thereon, and to see that the said collar with the said tag attached thereto is worn by the dog at all times. 
(Ord. of 4-7-70, § 1)  
Sec. 6-50. - Running at large. 
It shall be unlawful for the owner of any dog to permit the same to run at large within this city. 
(Ord. of 4-7-70, § 2)  
Sec. 6-51. - Sanitary enclosures. 
The owners or harborers of all dogs within this city are hereby required to keep the same within suitable enclosures and are further required to keep such enclosures sanitary and clean so as to prevent disagreeable odors arising therefrom, or the presence or breeding of flies, mosquitoes and other pests. 
(Ord. of 4-7-70, § 3)  
Sec. 6-52. - Nuisance prohibited. 
It shall be unlawful for the owner or harborer of any dog to permit the same to create a disturbance in the neighborhood or annoy any person or family or become a nuisance in any manner, particularly by reason of noises, odors, filthy conditions or the breeding of flies, mosquitoes and other pests. 
(Ord. of 4-7-70, § 3)  
Sec. 6-53. - Breeding restricted. 
It shall be unlawful for any person, owner of dogs, or otherwise, to keep and maintain the same for breeding purposes within the area of the city in violation of the zoning ordinance of the city. 
(Ord. of 4-7-70, § 4)  
Sec. 6-54. - Cruelty. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to torture, torment, unjustifiably injure, deprive of necessary sustenance, food or drink; or cruelly beat or needlessly mutilate any dog within the city or to cause or permit the same to be done. 
(Ord. of 4-7-70, § 5)  
Secs. 6-55—6-59. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 2. - IMPOUNDMENT 
 
Sec. 6-60. - Authorized. 
(a)  Any dog in violation of the provisions of this article may be seized and impounded by the animal control officer or any police officer of the city. Impoundment may be in any animal shelter designated by the mayor and board of aldermen. 
(b)  Any dangerous, fierce or vicious dog found in violation of the provisions of this article and cannot be safely taken up or impounded, such dog may be slain by any police officer. Further, any dog found to be severely injured or diseased may be disposed of in a humane manner by the animal control officer or chief of police. 
(Ord. of 4-7-70, § 2; Ord. of 4-17-90)  
Sec. 6-61. - Fees and charges. 
The following fees shall be charged for the impoundment of any dog under the provisions of this division: 
(1)  First redemption of a dog within calendar year ..... $10.00 
(2)  Second redemption of the same dog within calendar year ..... $25.00 
(3)  Third redemption of the same dog within calendar year ..... $50.00 
Whenever any dog is impounded, an additional fee of $5.00 per day shall be charged for each day or fraction thereof of impoundment for feeding and caring of said dog. 
(Ord. of 4-7-70, § 2; Ord. of 4-17-90)  
Sec. 6-62. - Redemption of unvaccinated dog. 
Any impounded dog which has not been vaccinated under this article shall be so vaccinated at the designated animal shelter prior to redemption by the owner. Any and all costs for such vaccination shall be paid in full by the owner prior to redemption. 
(Ord. of 4-7-70, § 2; Ord. of 4-17-90)  
Sec. 6-63. - Redemption by person other than owner. 
If the owner of any dog impounded under this division shall fail to redeem such dog within five days after such impoundment, any other person may, upon complying with the provisions of this division, redeem such dog from the pound and be the valid owner of such dog thereafter. 
(Ord. of 4-7-70, § 2; Ord. of 4-17-90)  
Sec. 6-64. - Disposition of unredeemed dogs. 
All dogs impounded under this division and which have not been redeemed or purchased as authorized by this division within five days of such impoundment, may be disposed of in a humane manner by the animal control officer or chief of police. 
(Ord. of 4-7-70, § 2; Ord. of 4-17-90)  
Secs. 6-65—6-80. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE V. - WILD AND DANGEROUS ANIMALS[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
Editor's note— An ordinance adopted September 21, 2010, did not specify manner of inclusion; hence, inclusion as article V, sections 6-81—6-85 is at the discretion of the editor. 
 
Sec. 6-81. - General purpose. 
The following regulations are for the purpose of promoting public health, safety, and general welfare of the citizens of the city, and to ensure the protection of citizens by regulating the control of wild, non-domestic, and dangerous animals within the city. This article shall not repeal any other existing ordinance not incompatible with the provisions of this article. 
(Ord. of 9-21-10)  
Sec. 6-82. - Regulated wild or dangerous animals. 
(a)  Definitions. The following definitions shall be used for the purposes of interpreting this article. For terms not defined below, the common usage of the term shall prevail. 
Animal means any live creature, both domestic and wild, excluding humans. "Animal" includes fowl, fish, and reptiles. 
Animal control officer means an employee of the city, designated by the city mayor and board of aldermen to administer and enforce the requirements of this article. "Animal control officer" includes, but is not limited to, officers of the city police department. 
Hybrid means any animal which contains any mix or percentage of a wild animal, or a mix or percentage of members of the canidae, felidae, or ursidae families. 
Inherently dangerous animal means any live member of the canidae, felidae, or ursidae families, including hybrids thereof, which, due to their inherent nature, may be considered dangerous to humans and which include: 
(1)  Canidae, including any member of the dog (canid) family not customarily domesticated by man, or any hybrids thereof, including wolf hybrids which are a cross between a wolf and a domestic dog, but not including domestic dogs (Canis Familiaris). 
(2)  Felidae, including any member of the cat family weighing over 15 pounds and not customarily domesticated by man, or any hybrids thereof, but not including domestic cats (Felis Catus). 
(3)  Ursidae, including any member of the bear family, or any hybrids thereof. 
Owner means any person having temporary or permanent custody of, possession of, breeding, exchanging, buying, selling, maintaining, keeping or permitting to be kept, sheltering or having charge of, harboring, exercising control over, or having property rights to, any animal controlled by this article. An animal shall be deemed to be harbored if it is fed or sheltered for three or more consecutive days. 
Wild animal means any live monkey, nonhuman primate, raccoon, skunk, fox, leopard, panther, tiger, lynx, alligator, crocodile, cayman, bear, sea mammal, poisonous snake, or any other warm blooded animal that can normally be found in the wild state. "Wild animal" also means any animal that would require a standard of care and control greater than that required for customary household pets sold by commercial pet shops or domestic farm animals. The term "wild animal" does not include domestic dogs, domestic cats, farm animals, rodents, and captive-bred species of common cage birds. 
(b)  Regulations and standards imposed. 
(1)  Keeping of inherently dangerous animals. It shall be unlawful for any person to keep an inherently dangerous animal within the city. The animal control officer shall order the removal of any inherently dangerous animals owned or harbored by anyone in possession of such animals within the city. 
(2)  Keeping of wild animals. It shall be unlawful for anyone to own or harbor a wild animal. The animal control officer shall order the removal of any wild animals owned or harbored by anyone in possession of such animals within the city. 
(3)  Exemptions. Traveling fairs, circuses, carnivals which are licensed by the United States Department of Agriculture (USDA) shall be exempt from this section, provided the duration of such presence shall be limited to a duration not to exceed 14 days annually within the boundaries of the city. Additionally, all non-profit animal sanctuaries licensed by the United States Department of Agriculture (USDA) shall be exempt from this section. All entities exempt pursuant to this section shall maintain liability insurance upon all animals within their control in the amount of not less than $1,000,000.00 at all times. 
(4)  Recapturing. The owner, including those allowed to possess such animals pursuant to the exemption stated above, of any inherently dangerous animal or wild animal shall reimburse the city for all costs incurred while attempting to recapture any escaped inherently dangerous animal or wild animal. If the animal is sheltered or euthanized by the animal control officer or his designee, the owner shall also pay these costs. 
(Ord. of 9-21-10)  
Sec. 6-83. - Permit required—Standards for permit. 
Any person or organization wishing to bring either wild animals or inherently dangerous animals into the city pursuant to subsection 6-82(b) shall first obtain a permit from the city animal control officer for the period in which the animals are to be present within the city. Before issuing the permit, the owner shall provide the animal control officer with the dates requested for the animals to be present, the type of animals to be present, their numbers, and proof of licensure by the United States Department of Agriculture to possess such animals. The owner must also maintain and provide the city with proof of liability insurance in the amount of at least $1,000,000.00. 
(Ord. of 9-21-10)  
Sec. 6-84. - Violations and penalties. 
Any person violating any provision of this article shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished by a fine of not less than $25.00 nor more than $1,000.00 or imprisonment in the county jail not to exceed 90 days, or by both such fine and imprisonment, unless otherwise provided for herein. Each day's violation shall be deemed a separate offense. 
(Ord. of 9-21-10)  
Sec. 6-85. - Administration and enforcement. 
(a)  The civil and criminal provisions of this article shall be enforced by the division of animal control and the city police department. 
(b)  Any police officer or animal control officer having probable cause that a person has violated a section of this article may, in lieu of obtaining a misdemeanor warrant for arrest of such suspect, issue to the person a written citation requiring the person to appear at a date and time in the municipal court to answer the charge or charges specified in the citation. 
(c)  It shall be a violation of this article to interfere with an animal control officer in the performance of his duties. 
(d)  It shall be allowable for an animal control officer to access any exterior area of private property for the purposes of securing and/or providing aid to any animal (s) found in violation of this article or found in circumstances that violate this article, so as to require enforcement. In the event that the property is enclosed with a fence or has other areas of hidden visibility that must be accessed, the animal control officer shall request the support of a police officer on-site before entering the fenced area. 
If the animal control officer shall determine that any of the provisions of this article are being violated, he shall notify in writing the person responsible for such violation, indicating the nature of the violation and ordering the action necessary to correct the violation within ten working days. In the event the violation poses an imminent threat, in the opinion of the animal control officer, to the life, safety, or property of any individual, the animal control officer may take such actions to correct the violation immediately and thereafter provide written notice to the owner of the violation. 
(Ord. of 9-21-10)  
Chapter 7 - BUILDINGS AND BUILDING REGULATIONS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Editor's note— To facilitate the inclusion of material, and at the discretion of the editor, the title of chapter 7 has been changed from "Building" to "Buildings and building regulations." 
Cross reference— Electricity, Ch. 11; air conditioning, § 11-65 et seq.; fire protection and prevention, Ch. 12; floodplain management, Ch. 12½; health and sanitation, Ch. 15; housing, Ch. 16; mobile homes, Ch. 19; planning and zoning, Ch. 25; plumbing and gas, Ch. 26; subdivisions and street extensions, Ch. 30; utilities, Ch. 35; zoning, Appendix A; house numbering, § 29-33 et seq. 
 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Sec. 7-1. - Fire limits—Inside city. 
The fire limits of the city are hereby established as follows, to wit: 
Commence at a point where the centerline of West Fulton Street intersects with the centerline of the Illinois Central Gulf Railroad, being the point of beginning. From said point of beginning proceed in an easterly direction along the centerline of West Fulton Street and East Fulton Street to a point where said centerline of Whitmire Alley to a point where said centerline intersects with the centerline of East Peace Street; thence proceed in an easterly direction along the centerline of East Peace Street to a point where said centerline intersects with the centerline of Telephone Alley; thence proceed in a northerly direction along the centerline of Telephone Alley to the north boundary line of East Center Street; thence proceed in a westerly direction along the north right-of-way of East Center Street to a point where said north right-of-way intersects with the centerline of Block 1, Madison Courthouse Square, being the east boundary line of Lots 1, 2, 3 and 4 of said Block 1; thence proceed in a northerly direction along said centerline, being the east boundary line of Blocks 1, 2, 3, and 4, to the centerline of East North Street; thence proceed in a westerly direction along the centerline of East North Street and West North Street to a point where said centerline intersects with the center line of the Illinois Central Gulf Railroad; and thence proceed in a southwesterly direction along the centerline of said Illinois Central Gulf Railroad right-of-way to the point of beginning. 
(Ord. of 6-3-58, § 6; Ord. of 4-26-88)  
Sec. 7-2. - Same—Outside city. 
(a)  Under and pursuant to the provision of section 21-25-21 of the Mississippi Code of 1972, a fire district adjoining the municipal boundaries of the City of Canton is hereby created. The area included therein and encompassed thereby be and the same is hereby designated and described as: 
All that part of Industrial Park Subdivision, No. 2, lying outside of the municipal boundaries of the City of Canton, Mississippi, according to and as shown by the map or plat of said subdivision which is on file and of record in Plat Book 6 at page 1 in the office of the chancery clerk of Madison County, Mississippi, reference to which is hereby expressly made in aid and as a part of this description. 
(b)  All municipal fire protection and prevention services, including the installation and maintenance of water mains and fire hydrants, and the furnishing of such available equipment and personnel as may be required for the prevention or extinguishment of fires is hereby extended to and established in said district on the same basis as if the same were located within the boundaries of the municipality. 
(Ord. of 11-16-76, §§ 1, 2) 
Editor's note— Codification of an ordinance of Nov. 16, 1976, nonamendatory of the Code, as § 7-2 was at the editor's discretion.  
Sec. 7-3. - Application for permit affecting property within urban renewal areas to be submitted to redevelopment authority for approval prior to issuance. 
Any and all applications for construction and/or building permits filed with the city clerk, affecting property within the urban renewal areas of the city, should be submitted to the Canton Redevelopment Authority for review and approval prior to the issuance of any construction and/or building permit. 
(Ord. of 9-15-87)  
Sec. 7-4. - Building permit application procedure. 
(a)  Policy. No building or other structure, including manufactured homes, shall be erected, altered, moved, added to, or structurally altered without a permit therefor. 
(b)  Procedure. Building permits shall be issued in accordance with the following provisions. 
(1)  Applications for building permits shall be completed, dated and signed by the property owner, and submitted to the building official. 
(2)  Applications for building permits which request a change in the zoning of any land, or request a variance or special exception from any of the provisions of the zoning ordinance, shall include a separate written request for such zoning change, variance or special exception, supported by such ether information specified in the zoning ordinance. Such applications shall be subject to the public notice, hearing, review and approval procedures specified in the zoning ordinance. 
(3)  Applications for building permits which require the subdivision of any land, or require the opening of a new public roadway, shall include a separate preliminary plat for such subdivision or roadway, prepared by a professional engineer or professional land surveyor registered in the State of Mississippi, supported by such other information specified in the subdivision ordinance. Such applications shall be subject to the public notice, hearing, review and approval procedures specified in the subdivision ordinance. 
(4)  Applications shall be accompanied by two complete sets of plans for all residential construction, and by three complete sets of plans and specifications for all commercial construction. Residential applications shall include an accurate plot plan reflecting the location of the structure, all set back lines, and other pertinent information. Commercial applications shall include a detailed site plan prepared by a professional engineer or professional land surveyor registered in the State of Mississippi, reflecting the location of the structure, all set back lines, all drives and parking areas, all drainage improvements, all utility services, existing and proposed contours, and other pertinent information, and detailed building plans and specifications prepared by a professional architect or professional engineer registered in the State of Mississippi, reflecting the foundation plan, floor plans, elevations, roofing, plumbing, electrical, HYAC, structural, and other pertinent Information. Residential plot plans and commercial site plans shall also reflect the current property ownership, land zoning and flood zone classification of the subject property and all adjoining properties. 
(5)  Applications shall be amended to include such other information as may be determined necessary and appropriate by the building official. 
(6)  Building official shall furnish a copy of all permit applications to the city clerk, utilities manager, public works director, city fire inspector, city engineer and city attorney for review, and shall solicit comments on all permit applications from other city department heads. If the application involves property located in the urban renewal area, a copy of same shall be furnished to the executive director of the redevelopment authority, if the application involves property located in the historic district, a copy of same shall be furnished to the chairman of the historic preservation commission. 
(7)  Building official shall assemble all continents made by the city clerk, utilities manager, public works director, city fire inspector, city engineer, city attorney, redevelopment executive director, and historic preservation commission, and shall furnish same to the applicant. The applicant, shall amend his application and/or plans to include such clarifications and/or additional information *quested, and shall then resubmit his application and/or plans to the building official for further review. If there were no comments, the building official shall proceed with processing the application. 
(8)  When all matters are in order, the building official shall notify the applicant that he is ready to issue the permit. The applicant shall then pay the permit fee to the City of Canton, and shall deliver such payment to the building official. Upon receipt of such payment, building official shall sign the permit application form, and shall furnish the applicant with a copy of the executed form, as confirmation that the permit is approved and as a written receipt for payment of the permit fee. 
(9)  Building official shall return one set of the approved plot plan, site plan, preliminary plat, building plan, specification, and/or other document to the applicant upon approval of the permit. The approved documents shall be kept on the site of the work, along with any approved amendments to same, for review and use by the city officials visiting the site. The remaining sets of the approved documents shall be retained on file by the building official for his files and use during the construction process. 
(10)  Building official shall prepare and issue a building permit form to the applicant upon approval of the permit application and receipt of the permit fee. Applicant shall post rich permit form on the construction site prior to initiating any work, and such form shall be readily visible from the public street adjoining the construction site. 
(Ord. of 5-7-96, Exh. A)  
Secs. 7-5—7-16. - Reserved.

A true and correct copy shall be kept on file in the office of the city clerk. 
Appendix "A"—Weights of Building Materials 
Appendix "B"—Recommended Schedule of Permit Fees 
B101—Permit Fees 
B102—Moving Fee 
B103—Demolition Fee 
B104—Penalties 
Appendix "D"—Standards for Demolition, 1997 Edition 
Appendix "H"—Manufactured Homes Tie Down Standards, 1997 Edition 
(Ord. of 3-5-68, § 1; Ord. of 12-1-87; Ord. of 12-2-97, § 1; Ord. of 1-30-98, § 1) 
State Law reference— Adoption of technical codes, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 3374-80.  
Sec. 7-17.1. - Reserved. 
Editor's note— Section 7-17.1 has been deleted by the editor, inasmuch as it appears to have been superseded by § 1 of an ordinance adopted 12-2-97. Said section pertained to amendments, and was derived from § 1 of an ordinance adopted Aug. 21, 1979; and an ordinance adopted Dec. 1, 1987. See the Code Comparative Table for further information.  
Sec. 7-18. - Conflicts. 
In the event of any conflict between the provisions of the code adopted by this article and applicable provisions of this Code of Ordinances, state law or city ordinances, rules or regulations, the provisions of this Code of Ordinances, state law or city ordinances, rules or regulations shall prevail and be controlling.  
Sec. 7-19. - Definitions. 
Whenever the word "municipality" or the word "city" is used in the code adopted by this article, it shall be construed to mean the City of Canton, Mississippi. 
Whenever the term "corporate counsel" or "city attorney" is used in the code adopted by this article, it shall be construed to mean the city attorney of this city. 
Whenever reference is made to the duties of certain officials named in this code adopted by this article, the designated officials of the City of Canton, Mississippi, who shall have duties corresponding to those named officials in said code shall be deemed to be the responsible officials insofar as enforcing the provisions of said code are concerned. 
(Ord. of 6-3-58, § 5; Ord. of 12-1-87)  
Sec. 7-20. - Penalty for violation. 
Any person who shall violate any provision of the ordinance and code adopted by the provisions of this article shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor, and shall be punished as provided by section 1-4 of this Code. Each day such violation continues shall be deemed a separate offense. 
(Ord. of 3-1-66, § 1)  
Sec. 7-21. - Reserved. 
Editor's note— An ordinance of December 1, 1987, amended the permit fees as set out in the building code; therefore, the permit fees are now included in § 7-17.1 instead of § 7-21.

III, §§ 7-31—7-41, which provisions derived from an ordinance of April 1, 1980, have been redesignated as Div. 2 of Art. III. 
 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY

A true and correct copy shall be kept on file in the office of the city clerk.

B101.1—Initial Fee

DIVISION 2. - MECHANICAL REGULATORY BOARD[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
Note— See the editor's footnote to Art. III of this chapter. 
 
Sec. 7-31. - Organization. 
(a)  Established; members; appointment. There is hereby established a mechanical licensing board, which shall hereafter be referred to as the board. The board shall consist of seven members, and shall be constituted as follows, to wit: 
(1)  One air conditioning contractor to be appointed by the board of aldermen. 
(2)  Two master electricians to be appointed by the board of aldermen. 
(3)  Two master plumbers to be appointed by the board of aldermen. 
(4)  One representative from the Madison County Board of Health Office. 
(5)  One representative from Canton Municipal Utilities to be appointed by the Canton Municipal Utility Board. 
The mechanical inspector referred to in section 7-40 of this division shall attend all regular and special meetings of the mechanical licensing board but he shall not have a vote in the business conducted by said board. 
(b)  Term of office. The term of office for the members of the board shall be a two-year period. 
(c)  Members to be residents and/or perform city regulated services. No member of the board in regard to the appointments listed hereinabove in subsections (a)(1) through (3) shall be appointed to the subject board unless he or she be a resident of the city and/or regularly perform services regulated hereby within the city. 
(d)  Reappointment. Each member of the board may serve two consecutive terms after which he shall not be eligible for reappointment for a period of at least one year. The inspector shall be a permanent member of the board. 
(e)  Chairman; vice-chairman. The board shall select one of its members to serve as chairman, who shall preside at all meetings, and a vice-chairman who shall preside in the absence of the chairman. 
(f)  Authority. The board may conduct examinations, grant licenses, receive complaints, conduct hearings, revoke licenses, make investigations and recommendations to the mayor and board of aldermen from time to time for amendments and changes in the electrical, plumbing, gas and air conditioning regulations and procedures. 
(g)  Meetings. Regular meetings of the mechanical licensing board shall be held as determined by the board and special meetings may be called at any time by the chairman by giving at least one day notice thereof. The board shall keep minutes of all of its proceedings. 
(Ord. of 4-1-80, § 4)  
Sec. 7-32. - License—Required for electrical or appliance work. 
From and after the effective date of this division, it shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to engage in electrical work, the installation or connecting of appliances without first obtaining a license so to do from the city building and permit department, as hereinafter set forth. 
(Ord. of 4-1-80, § 1)  
Sec. 7-33. - Same—Application. 
Any person, firm or corporation desiring to engage in electrical work, the business of plumbing or gas fitting, or both, or air conditioning, shall before doing so, file his application with the licensing board setting forth the facts as provided for on the application, which shall show his business, training, and qualifications; which application shall be passed upon by the licensing board; and he shall be subject to such examination as the board shall deem advisable. 
(Ord. of 4-1-80, § 2)  
Sec. 7-34. - Same—Eligibility. 
Any person may apply for electricians', plumbers', gas fitters' or air conditioners' licenses provided he meets the following requirements: 
(1)  An applicant for master electricians', plumbers', gas fitters' or air conditioners' license shall have had at least five years experience in the business for which he is applying, or shall be a graduate of a trade school, technical school or college of recognized standing and, in addition, shall have had one year of practical experience in the operation of the business for which he is applying. 
(2)  The applicant shall furnish at least five letters from businessmen attesting to the applicant's experience, character and dependability. 
(3)  All applicants shall be required to satisfactorily pass the examination as hereinafter provided, except that all licensed electricians, plumbers, gas fitters or air conditioning contractors who hold licenses as such shall, at the effective date of this article, continue in the same classification without examination unless violations are cited as hereinafter provided. 
(Ord. of 4-1-80, § 7)  
Sec. 7-35. - Same—Renewal; suspension upon death of any master electrician, plumber, gas fitter, etc. 
The holder of any master electrician, plumbing, gas or air conditioning certificate shall renew same as provided by the renewal of other licenses by the Code. Holders of certificates not renewed prior to February first may be required to take the examination prior to reissuance of a license. In the event of the death of any master electrician, plumber, gas or air conditioning contractor, his license shall be immediately suspended. No company or business can then operate under his license. 
(Ord. of 4-1-80, § 6)  
Sec. 7-36. - Application for examination; fee. 
All applications for examination for licenses shall be made to the inspector on forms which shall be provided by the inspector at least 30 days prior to the examination. All certificates of approval shall be signed and issued by the inspector once approved by the licensing board. The applicant shall file with his application, a fee of $50.00. This fee applies also to any re-examination necessary due to failure of the first examination. 
(Ord. of 4-1-80, § 5)  
Sec. 7-37. - Approval of examination and minimum score; revocation of license; reissuance. 
(a)  Examination procedure. The examination for master electricians', plumbers', gas fitters' and air conditioning license shall be prepared by the inspector and approved by the licensing board. All applicants shall be required to obtain a minimum of 70 percent total to pass the examination. In the event of failure of an applicant to pass the examination, he may be permitted to take an additional examination after 120 days have expired. There shall be no limit as to the number of examinations a person shall be allowed to take, but each reexamination shall be subject to the same fees as herebefore set out and no refunds shall be made. 
(b)  Revocation. Any certificate granted under this article or which may be in force at the time that this article is passed may be revoked by the board if the holder of the certificate of license violates any ordinance or laws relating to electrical, plumbing or gas installations, or air conditioning installation, or should he permit the use of his license to allow a nonlicensed person to directly or indirectly use his license in obtaining permits for the installation of plumbing, electrical installation, gas installation or air conditioning installation. Such party shall be given full hearing, and the board shall fully satisfy themselves as to the violation involved. 
(c)  Reissuance. When a certificate is revoked, a new certificate shall not be granted to the same person, firm or corporation for a period of at least 30 days or until such person, firm, or corporation shall have corrected any faulty construction or other violations. Should the board deem it advisable, before reissuing the certificate, it may require that the party involved be required to take the examination as heretofore provided in this division. 
(Ord. of 4-1-80, § 8)  
Sec. 7-38. - Required supervision of master electrician, plumber, gas fitter, etc., required. 
No individual, firm, partnership or corporation shall engage in the business of installation, repairing or altering of electrical work, plumbing, gas or air conditioning installations unless the electrical, plumbing, gas and air conditioning work performed in the course of such business is under the supervision of a licensed master electrician, plumber, gas fitter, or air conditioning contractor. 
(Ord. of 4-1-80, § 3)  
Sec. 7-39. - Bond; certificate of insurance. 
(a)  Before said certificate or license shall be delivered to a successful applicant, he shall post a bond conditioned upon the faithful performance of any and all work authorized by said license in strict accordance with ordinances of the city. And in addition thereto, any person, firm or corporation desiring to engage in the business of electrical work, plumbing, gas fitting, or both, or air conditioning shall, before doing so, file with the inspector of the city, a certificate of liability insurance, issued by an insurance company duly authorized to do business in the state, in an amount not less than $25,000.00 for injury to any one person, and $50,000.00 property damage, covering all phases of the operation of his or its business, including the operation of automobiles. 
(b)  Such insurance policies shall be noncancellable, except after ten days written notice to the inspector. Failure to provide such insurance coverage shall result in the cancellation of electrical, plumbing or gas installation, or air conditioning license. 
(Ord. of 4-1-80, § 9)  
Sec. 7-40. - Inspector. 
(a)  Office created. There is hereby created an office of mechanical inspector and he shall be one and the same as electrical inspector, plumbing inspector, gas inspector and air conditioning inspector. 
(b)  Oath. The mechanical inspector shall take an oath of office and shall have full police powers under the ordinances of the city for carrying out of the purposes for which they are adopted. 
(c)  Assistants. He shall be furnished with such assistants as shall be necessary to carry out the purposes of the ordinances and his assistants shall have the same power of enforcement as the inspector. 
(d)  Utility board. The office of inspector shall be under the Canton Municipal Utility Commission Board and work in conjunction with the department of building and permits of the city. 
(e)  Bond. The inspector and his assistants shall be bonded in the sum of $2,000.00, same to be continued upon the faithful performance of his duties and indemnifying the city against all losses or damage arising from the negligent use of public property entrusted to him or arising from suits for injury or damages caused by defective or unsanitary work approved by him. 
(f)  Qualifications. He shall be a man of recognized knowledge of the business for which he is appointed. He shall not be engaged nor interested directly or indirectly in any electrical, plumbing, gas or air conditioning business, nor any manufacturer of sewerage materials or plumbing supplies. 
(Ord. of 4-1-80, § 10)  
Sec. 7-41. - Violation; penalties. 
Any person, firm or corporation who violates, neglects or refuses to comply with, or resists the enforcement of any of the provisions of this article shall on conviction be fined not less than $50.00 or more than $300.00 for each offense, or imprisoned in the city jail not to exceed 90 days or by both such fine and imprisonment. Each day a violation is permitted to exist shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. of 4-1-80, § 11)  
Secs. 7-42—7-60. - Reserved.
