The giving of such permission shall be considered compliance with the provisions of section 17-25. 
(Ord. of 5-2-00, § VI)  
Sec. 17-27. - Disposal of junked vehicles; redemption. 
(a)  If such public nuisance is not abated by the owner or occupant after notice is given in accordance with this article, official action shall be taken by the city to abate such nuisance. Junked vehicles or parts thereof shall be impounded until lawfully claimed or disposed of in accordance with MCA 1972, §§ 63-23-1—63-23-11. 
(b)  Vehicles so impounded shall be held for 90 days and thereafter shall be disposed of with all rights of ownership being forfeited. Anytime prior to the expiration of the 90 days, the record title holder shall be allowed to redeem the vehicle upon the payment of all costs including towing, storage and other such administrative costs as may be determined. 
(Ord. of 5-2-00, § VII)  
Sec. 17-28. - Authority to enforce. 
The building official, or his designees, may enter upon private property for the purposes specified in this article to examine vehicles or parts thereof, obtain information as to the identity of vehicles and to remove or cause the removal of a vehicle or parts thereof declared to be a nuisance pursuant to this article. The board of aldermen shall have the authority to issue all orders necessary to enforce this article. 
(Ord. of 5-2-00, § VIII)  
Chapter 18 - LICENSES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Alcoholic beverages, Ch. 4; beer and wine, § 4-27 et seq.; taxicab drivers permit, § 32-34 et seq.; peddlers, Ch. 24. 
 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Secs. 18-1—18-15. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - LOCAL PRIVILEGE TAXES[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference— Poolroom, billiard halls, § 5-28 et seq.; electricians, § 11-15 et seq.; plumbers, § 26-26 et seq.; gas fitters, § 26-50. 
State Law reference— Local privilege tax law, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 9696-01. 
 
Sec. 18-16. - Adoption of state local code. 
The state local privilege tax code, Mississippi Code Annotated, Sections 9696-01—9696-235, is hereby adopted, levied and imposed as the privilege tax code of the city. 
(Code 1930, § 274) 
State Law reference— Imposition of privilege taxes, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 9696-01.  
Sec. 18-17. - Violation of article provisions. 
Any person violating any of the provisions of this article shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and on conviction thereof shall be fined not more than $500.00, or imprisoned not exceeding six months, or by both such fine and imprisonment. Such fine and imprisonment shall be in addition to any other penalty imposed by any particular section of this article or applicable provision of state law. Any person failing to pay the privilege taxes imposed by this article, and to obtain a license as required, but pursuing the business for which a privilege tax is imposed without procuring such license, may be proceeded against by suit, in addition to being dealt with criminally. The tax collector may seize and sell any property of such person liable for such tax and penalty, in the same manner as he may distrain and sell property of other taxpayers delinquent for the payment of ad valorem taxes due on personal property. 
(Code 1930, §§ 279, 281) 
State Law reference— Similar state law, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 9696-228.  
Sec. 18-18. - Application of other provisions. 
All privilege licenses provided for by this article shall be granted subject to any other applicable provision of this Code, state law or city ordinance, rule or regulation.  
Sec. 18-19. - Collection, payment of taxes. 
The tax collector shall collect, and all persons liable therefor shall pay to the tax collector, all privilege taxes levied and imposed by the provisions of this article before the beginning of the business for which a privilege tax is required and annually thereafter. 
(Code 1930, § 270) 
State Law reference— Where license obtained, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 9696-206; application, § 9696-207.  
Sec. 18-20. - Issuance. 
The tax collector shall, upon payment of the privilege tax levied and imposed by this article, issue a privilege license evidencing such payment. 
(Code 1930, § 270) 
State Law reference— Issuance of license, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 9696-208.  
Sec. 18-21. - Duty of licensee to furnish information. 
Any person, when duly and legally directed by the mayor and board of aldermen to produce and exhibit to the board any information or statement in connection with the use or sale, of any object or thing subject to regulation by the city, shall produce or exhibit such information or statement.  
Sec. 18-22. - Separate businesses, locations. 
Any person engaging in more than one of the businesses for which a privilege tax is imposed shall pay separately the privilege tax imposed upon each separate business, except as may be otherwise specifically provided by the privilege tax code. Furthermore, if the business taxed is carried on at two or more separate locations or places, a separate license for each location of such business shall be obtained. 
(Code 1930, § 272) 
State Law reference— Similar state law, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 9696-209.  
Sec. 18-23. - Effect of change in nature of business. 
When a privilege license is issued under the provisions of this article to carry on a certain line of business, and after the issuance of said license, the licensee shall so change or alter his business as to bring it under a classification for which a higher license tax is required, he shall before making such change, deliver his license to the tax collector, together with a written and signed statement as to the nature of such proposed change, and shall pay to the tax collector the proper additional license tax. The tax collector shall thereupon cancel the old license and shall issue to the licensee a new and appropriate license. 
(Code 1930, § 278) 
State Law reference— Increased business, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 9696-210.  
Sec. 18-24. - Display. 
Each privilege license issued under the provisions of this article shall be displayed in a conspicuous part of the place of business for which the license was issued. In the event the licensee does not have a fixed, permanent location, or in the event the business is such that the license cannot be displayed as required by this section, the licensee shall have such license in his actual possession at the time of carrying on such business. 
(Code 1930, § 273) 
State Law reference— Similar state law, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 9696-213.  
Sec. 18-25. - Transferability. 
All privilege licenses issued pursuant to the provisions of this article shall be a personal privilege and shall not be transferable to any other person or location. 
(Code 1930, § 277) 
State Law reference— Similar state law, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 9696-215.  
Sec. 18-26. - Unlawful business. 
The issuance of a privilege license, as the payment of a tax therefor, shall not make lawful any business, employment, transaction, article or device or the operation thereof, contrary to any provision of this Code, state law, or city ordinance, rule or regulation. 
State Law reference— Similar state law, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 9696-215.  
Sec. 18-27. - Expiration of licenses. 
Pursuant to Section 6 of Senate Bill No. 2081, enacted by the Legislature of the State of Mississippi, in its Regular 1988 Session, any and all privilege licenses issued by the City of Canton, Mississippi, after the effective date of the act, being the first day of July, 1988, shall expire one year from and after the date of issuance. 
(Ord. of 7-19-88) 
Editor's note— An ordinance of July 19, 1988, did not specifically amend the Code; therefore, inclusion as § 18-27 was at the discretion of the editor.  
Secs. 18-28—18-36. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE III. - COIN-OPERATED MACHINES 
 
Sec. 18-37. - Nonapplication of article. 
This article shall not apply to any machine operated for gambling purposes, to any machine kept at a regular place of business of distributors or manufacturers for sale or lease without being operated, or to any pool table operated at a place of business commonly known as a pool hall or billiards parlor when the gross income from the operation of such pool table is taxable under the state sales tax law. 
(Ord. of 7-7-70, § 7)  
Sec. 18-38. - Definition. 
For the purposes of this article, the phrase "slot amusement machine" shall mean any mechanical device or contrivance which is operated, played, worked, manipulated or used by inserting or depositing any coin, slug, token or thing of value, in which may be seen any picture or heard any music, or wherein any game may be played or any form of diversion had. 
(Ord. of 7-7-70, § 2)  
Sec. 18-39. - Taxes levied. 
There is hereby levied and imposed upon each person engaging in the business of owning or placing on location for the purpose of operation any slot amusement machine which is located within the city an annual license tax according to the following schedules: 
(a)  For each machine wherein may be seen any picture or heard any music, a license tax for each such machine in the sum of $9.00. 
(b)  For each machine not elsewhere specifically taxed in this section, wherein or whereby any game may be played or any form of diversion had, a license tax for each machine in the sum of $15.00. 
(c)  For each machine, not elsewhere specifically taxed in this section, wherein or by means of which children may obtain a ride upon a "hobby horse" or figure of any animal, or upon the figure of a boat, airplane, rocket or other machine, a license tax of $6.00 for each machine. 
(Ord. of 7-7-70, § 1) 
State Law reference— Slot amusement machine tax, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 9418-01 et seq.; authority to levy, § 9418-03.  
Sec. 18-40. - Vending machines—Generally. 
There is hereby levied and imposed upon each person engaging in the business of owning or placing on location for the purpose of operation, or each person permitting to be operated in his place of business any automatic vending machine where any service is rendered or where is kept within the machine any article of merchandise to be obtained by depositing therein any token, coin or coins, not otherwise taxed by this division, an annual tax as follows: 
(a)  For each machine requiring the deposit of a token, coin or coins of less than $0.05 value ..... $2.50 
(b)  For each machine requiring the deposit of a token, coin or coins of $0.05 and less than $0.10 value ..... 5.00 
(c)  For each machine requiring the deposit of a token, coin or coins of $0.10 and less than $0.20 value ..... 7.50 
(d)  For each machine requiring the deposit of a token, coin or coins of $0.20 or more value ..... 10.00 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 9426-01(c); authority to levy, § 9426-02.  
Sec. 18-41. - Same—Exemption. 
Vending machines requiring deposits of less than $0.05 and vending food products only shall be exempt from the provisions of section 18-40 and no privilege tax shall be required to be paid when such machines are sponsored by local nonprofit civic service clubs or any other organization either incorporated or unincorporated and existing and operating under the state law, when such clubs or organizations expend the proceeds from such machines for charitable purposes only. 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 9426-01(c).  
Sec. 18-42. - Postage vending machines. 
There is hereby imposed and levied upon each person operating, owning or permitting to be operated in his place of business any automatic or slot vending machine or other devices dispensing or selling postage stamps, for each such machine an annual tax of $2.00. 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 9426-01(a); authority to levy, § 9426-02.  
Sec. 18-43. - Cigarette vending machines. 
There is hereby levied and imposed upon each person operating, owning or permitting to be operated in his place of business any automatic or slot vending machine wherein is kept within the machine cigarettes on which the specific privilege tax of selling such articles of merchandise at retail has been paid by the owner of the machine or the owner of the place of business where such machine is operated to be obtained by depositing therein any token, coin or coins, for each such machine an annual tax of $2.50. 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 9426-01(b); authority to levy, § 9426-02.  
Sec. 18-44. - Weighing machines. 
There is hereby levied and imposed upon each person operating, owning or permitting to be operated in his place of business any automatic or slot weighing machine, for each such machine an annual tax of $2.00. 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 9426-01(a); authority to levy, § 9426-02.  
Sec. 18-45. - Application. 
Every person engaged in the business of owning or placing on location for the purpose of operation within the city any slot amusement machine shall file an application for license with the city clerk on forms furnished for that purpose. The application shall contain such information as may be required by the clerk and shall be accompanied by the remittance for the amount of tax and any penalty required. 
(Ord. of 7-7-70, § 3)  
Sec. 18-46. - When due. 
The tax levied by this article shall be due and payable annually on the first day of January. 
(Ord. of 7-7-70, § 4)  
Sec. 18-47. - Pro rata payment. 
The amount of the license tax to be paid under this article for a period of less than 12 months shall be that proportionate amount of the annual license tax that the number of months, or fractional part thereof remaining until January 1, next bears to 12 months. 
(Ord. of 7-7-70, § 4)  
Sec. 18-48. - Expiration. 
All licenses issued under the provisions of this article shall expire on the 31st day of December next following their date of issuance. 
(Ord. of 7-7-70, § 4)  
Sec. 18-49. - Renewal. 
A license issued under the provisions of this article may be renewed without penalty during the month of January next following its expiration. 
(Ord. of 7-7-70, § 4)  
Sec. 18-50. - Display. 
The city clerk shall issue a license on a form to be prescribed by the clerk, which license shall be securely affixed or attached to the machine to which it applies in such a manner as to be readily visible and shall be affixed before the machine is operated or played. The absence of a proper license or sticker affixed to the machine shall be prima facie evidence of failure to pay the tax levied for operation of the machine. 
(Ord. of 7-7-70, § 5)  
Sec. 18-51. - Penalty for nonpayment. 
Any person engaged in the business of owning or placing on location in the city for the purpose of operation, any slot amusement machine without the payment of the tax imposed herein, or without affixing such license to such machine, shall be liable for the amount of tax and 50 percent of the amount of the tax as penalty. 
(Ord. of 7-7-70, § 6)  
Chapter 19 - MOBILE HOMES[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Building, Ch. 7; electricity, Ch. 11; fire prevention and protection, Ch. 12; garbage and trash, Ch. 14; health and sanitation, Ch. 15; housing, Ch. 16; planning and zoning, Ch. 25; plumbing and gas, Ch. 26; streets and sidewalks, Ch. 29; traffic regulations, Ch. 33; zoning, Appendix A. 
 
Sec. 19-1. - Use as residence restricted. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to establish, construct, erect, locate, keep or maintain or to cause to be established, constructed, erected, located, kept or maintained, any mobile home within the city, except in a mobile home park provided, for the purpose of utilizing the same as a place of residence or for the purpose of leasing or renting the same to others for utilization as a place of residence. 
(Ord. of 11-5-63, § 1)  
Sec. 19-2. - Temporary permit. 
Any person desiring to establish, construct, erect, locate, keep or maintain a mobile home within the city other than in an area in a mobile home park specifically permitted, may petition the mayor and board of aldermen for an exception or variance from the provisions of this chapter, and upon good cause shown for so doing, the mayor and board of aldermen, may grant such exception or variation after first determining that such exception or variation will not impair an adequate supply of light and air to the adjacent property or impair established property values within the surrounding area or in any other respect impair the health, safety, comfort, moral or welfare of the city. 
(Ord. of 11-5-63, § 3)  
Chapter 20 - MOTOR VEHICLES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Vehicle equipment, § 33-91 et seq.; two wheel motor vehicles, § 33-187 et seq.; placing handbills in vehicles, § 3-24; automobile graveyards, § 17-18 et seq. 
 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Sec. 20-1. - Storage of motor vehicles. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful to store for sale, transfer, future use or repair, any motor vehicle in any areas within the municipal boundaries of the City of Canton, Mississippi, which are presently, or may hereinafter be classified, for any single-family residential use or multifamily residential use. 
(b)  The mayor and board of aldermen are hereby authorized and empowered on their own motion or upon receipt of any affidavit from any citizen of the City of Canton, Mississippi, requesting the mayor and board of aldermen to so act, to give notice to the owner of property upon which any violation hereunder exists requesting the abatement and/or correction of the violation or violations. Said notice shall be received by the owner of such real property by U.S. Registered Mail or Certified Mail, Return Receipt Requested, received by the addressee only, at least 21 days before the date of a public hearing or by service of notice by a police officer of the City of Canton, Mississippi, at least 21 days before the date of a public hearing, or if the property owner be unknown or his address unknown, then by notice published three times in a newspaper having a general circulation within the municipality with the first publication at least 21 days prior to the date of such public hearing. 
(c)  If at said public hearing, it is found that the violation or violations have not been corrected, and/or abated, the property owner shall be guilty of a misdemeanor upon conviction and shall be punished by fine in an amount not less than $10.00 and not more than $50.00 and provided further that each day during which said event shall occur or continue, is deemed to be a separate offense. 
(Ord. of 12-5-89) 
Cross reference— An ordinance of December 5, 1989, did not specifically amend the Code; therefore, inclusion as § 20-1 was at the discretion of the editor.  
Secs. 20-2—20-15. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - AD VALOREM TAXES[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference— Taxation, Ch. 31. 
State Law reference— Motor vehicle ad valorem taxes, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 10007-01 et seq. 
 
Sec. 20-16. - Adoption of tax. 
The mayor and board of aldermen hereby elect to make use of and adopt the assessment schedule for motor vehicles prepared and provided by the state tax commission as the basis for the assessment and collection of ad valorem taxes on motor vehicles located within its jurisdiction. 
State Law reference— Motor vehicle ad valorem assessment schedule prepared by state tax commission, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 10007-10.  
Sec. 20-17. - Collection. 
The county tax collector is hereby authorized to collect the motor vehicle ad valorem taxes of the city at the same time and in the same manner that the county tax collector collects the county and state ad valorem taxes on such motor vehicles. Such collector shall receive fees for his services in making such collections as determined by the mayor and board of aldermen. 
State Law reference— Collection of ad valorem taxes by county tax assessor for city, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 10007-15.  
Chapter 21 - NOISE[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Dogs as nuisances, § 6-52; mufflers required on motor vehicles, § 33-98. 
State Law reference— Authority to regulate noise, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 3374-124. 
 
Sec. 21-1. - Prohibited generally. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to make, continue, or cause to be made or continued any loud, unnecessary, or unusual noise or any noise which either annoys, disturbs, injures, or endangers the comfort, repose, health, peace or safety of others, within the city.  
Sec. 21-2. - Radios, phonographs, etc. 
The using, operating, or permitting to be played, used, or operated, any radio receiving set, television set, musical instrument, phonograph, or other machine or device for the producing or reproducing of sound, in such manner as to disturb the peace, quiet, and comfort of the neighboring inhabitants, or at any time with louder volume than is necessary for convenient hearing for the person or persons who are in the room, vehicle, or chamber in which such machine or device is operated and who are voluntary listeners thereto shall be deemed a violation of this chapter. The operation of any such set, instrument, phonograph, machine, or device between the hours of 12:00 p.m. and 7:00 a.m. in such a manner as to be plainly audible at a distance of 50 feet from the building, structure, or vehicle in which it is located, shall be prima facie evidence of a violation of this section. 
(Ord. of 10-6-32, § 1)  
Sec. 21-3. - Yelling, shouting. 
Yelling, shouting, hooting, whistling, or singing on the public streets, particularly between the hours of 11:00 p.m. and 7:00 a.m. or at any time or place so as to annoy or disturb the quiet, comfort, or repose of persons in any office, or in any dwelling, hotel, or other type of residence, or of any persons in the vicinity shall be deemed a violation of this chapter. 
Cross reference— Peddlers, Ch. 24.  
Sec. 21-4. - Loading, unloading, opening boxes. 
The creating of a loud and excessive noise in connection with loading or unloading any vehicle or the opening and destruction of bales, boxes, crates and containers shall be deemed a violation of this chapter.  
Sec. 21-5. - Pile drivers, hammers, etc. 
The operation between the hours of 10:00 p.m. and 7:00 a.m. of any pile driver, steamshovel, pneumatic hammer, derrick, steam or electric hoist or other appliance, the use of which is attended by loud or unusual noise shall be deemed a violation of this chapter.  
Sec. 21-6. - Horns, warning devices. 
The sounding of any horn or other warning device on any automobile, motorcycle, or other vehicle on any street or public place of the city, except as a danger warning; the creating by means of any such warning device of any unreasonably loud or harsh sound; and the sounding of any such device for an unnecessary and unreasonable period of time, and the use of such warning device when traffic for any reason is held up shall be deemed a violation of this chapter. 
Cross reference— Horns and warning devices, § 33-97.  
Sec. 21-7. - Animals, fowl. 
The keeping of any animal or bird which by causing frequent or long, continued noise shall disturb the comfort or repose of any person in the vicinity shall be deemed a violation of this chapter. 
Cross reference— Animals and fowl generally, Ch. 6.  
Sec. 21-8. - Defect in vehicle or load. 
The use of any automobile, motorcycle, or vehicle so out of repair, so loaded or in such manner as to create loud and unnecessary grating, grinding, rattling, or other noise shall be deemed a violation of this chapter.  
Sec. 21-9. - Blowers. 
The operation of any noise-creating blower or power fan or any internal combustion engine, the operation of which causes noise due to the explosion of operating gases or fluids, unless the noise from such blower or fan is muffled and such engine is equipped with a muffler device sufficient to deaden such noise shall be deemed a violation of this chapter.  
Sec. 21-10. - Screeching of tires. 
The operation of any motor vehicle in such a way as to cause the tires thereof to screech except where the same is necessarily caused in an emergency in an attempt by the operator to avoid an accident or the causing of damage or injury shall be deemed a violation of this chapter.  
Chapter 22 - OFFENSES AND MISCELLANEOUS PROVISIONS  
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Sec. 22-1. - Adoption of state misdemeanors. 
All acts which are classed as misdemeanors under and by virtue of the laws of the state are hereby adjudged to be violations of this Code and ordinances of the city when committed within the corporate limits of the city. The penalties which are imposed by state law for such violations are hereby adopted as the penalties for such violation within the city. 
(Code 1930, § 181) 
State Law reference— Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 3374-124 authorizes the adoption of an ordinance prohibiting any act constituting a misdemeanor under state law, whereas § 3374-78 provides that state misdemeanors shall be offenses against municipalities without further action by the municipality.  
Sec. 22-2. - Pawnbrokers to make daily reports to the chief of police. 
Every pawnbroker in the city is hereby required to make daily reports in writing to the chief of police. Said reports shall show name of person selling or pawning any article, color, residence, articles, description and amount. 
(Code 1930, § 267)  
Sec. 22-3. - Disorderly house. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to keep a disorderly house in the city by making, causing or allowing to be made therein, loud or improper noises, or by collecting therein drunken, noisy and disorderly persons. 
State Law reference— Bawdy houses considered disorderly houses, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 2333.  
Sec. 22-4. - Disorderly conduct. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to be guilty of any offense which shall constitute any disorderly conduct as provided by state law. 
State Law reference— Disorderly conduct generally, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 2087.3 et seq.  
Sec. 22-5. - Escape prohibited. 
Any person lawfully detained in jail or in custody of a law officer who shall escape from such detention or custody shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor. 
State Law reference— Escape generally, Miss Code Ann. 1942, § 2137 et seq.  
Sec. 22-6. - Aiding escape. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to aid any person who has been arrested or detained by any police officer to escape, or to knowingly aid any person who has violated any provision of this Code or ordinance of the city to escape before arrest. 
State Law reference— Aiding escape, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 2130 et seq.  
Secs. 22-7—22-12. - Reserved. 
Editor's note— An ordinance adopted January 2, 2007, repealed the former sections 22-7—22-12 in their entirety, which pertained to Sunday sales—Definition of "person", prohibition of sales; exceptions; sales in certain establishments; certain sales and carrying of advertisement by communications media not prohibited penalties for violations, and injunction to restrain violation and costs, respectively, and derived from an ordinance adopted May 20, 1986.  
Sec. 22-13. - Standing, loitering, etc., in public places. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to stand, loiter, walk or run upon any street, park, sidewalk or public place or any portion of private property which has been set aside by the owner thereof for the use of his customers and/or the public so as to obstruct free passage for other persons after having been requested to move on by a police officer. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person to loiter or prowl in a place at a time or in a manner which is not usual for law abiding individuals under circumstances that warrant alarm for the safety of persons or property in the vicinity, after having been requested by a police officer to identify himself or herself and explain his or her presence. 
(c)  Any person violating any of the provisions of this section shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, and on conviction thereof shall be fined not more than $500.00 or imprisoned, not to exceed 30 days, or by both such fine and imprisonment. 
(Ord. of 7-16-85, §§ 1—3)  
Sec. 22-14. - Reserved. 
Editor's note— At the discretion of the editor, an ordinance adopted December 20, 2011, has been treated as repealing the provisions of the former section 22-14, which pertained to smoking in public buildings owned and operated by the city, and derived from an ordinance adopted July 16, 1991. 
 For current provisions pertaining to smoking in public places, the user's attention is directed to article XIII of this chapter.  
Sec. 22-15. - Use or possession of tobacco by minors prohibited. 
(a)  Definitions. 
Educational activity: A school sponsored event within the city for athletic, academic, social or entertainment purposes, attended by students, including school transportation to and from, regardless of whether such activity is held on educational property. 
Educational property: Any public or private elementary or secondary school building or school bus, public or private campus, grounds, recreational area, athletic field, or other property owned, used or operated by a school board or board of trustees, or board of directors for the administration of any public or private educational institution within the corporate limits of the city. 
Tobacco products: Any tobacco cigarette, cigar, pipe, tobacco, smokeless tobacco or any other form of tobacco product which may be used for smoking, chewing, inhaling or ingesting by any other means. 
Use or possession: The smoking, chewing, oral consumption, spitting, inhaling, other ingestion of any tobacco products or the product, or the possession of a cigarette, cigar or other tobacco product, or any container of tobacco spittle. 
(b)  Use or possession by minors. No person under 18 years of age shall have in his or her possession or use any tobacco products within the operative limits of the city. 
(c)  Use or possession by students. No student of any high school, junior high or elementary school shall have in his or her possession or use any tobacco product on any educational property or at any educational activity within the corporate limits of the city. 
(d)  Penalty. Violation of this section is punishable by a fine not to exceed $100.00 and/or public service as ordered by any municipal, justice court, county, youth court, or other judge of competent jurisdiction. 
(Ord. of 1-19-99, §§ 1—4)  
Sec. 22-16. - Sentencing of habitual criminals to maximum term of imprisonment. 
Every person convicted in the municipal court of the city, of a misdemeanor (excluding traffic violations), who shall have been previously convicted twice within the same calendar year of any misdemeanor (excluding traffic violations), upon charges separately brought and arising out of separate incidents at different times, shall be sentenced to a maximum term of imprisonment prescribed for such misdemeanor; and, that such sentence shall not be reduced or suspended nor shall such person be eligible for probation. 
(Ord. of 10-6-98)  
Sec. 22-16.1. - Block parties. 
(a)  Purpose. The regulations contained in this section are ordained and required for the public health, safety, morals, standards, good order, convenience and general welfare of the community. It is the intention of this section to establish reasonable limits on block parties within the city limits, and to provide a regulatory framework for permitting block parties. 
(b)  Public conduct during block parties. 
(1)  All laws and ordinances are still in effect during an approved block party. 
(2)  The police department shall have the authority, when reasonably necessary, to prohibit or restrict the parking of vehicles along a highway or city street or part thereof constituting a part of the location of a block party. 
(c)  Guidelines and requirements. Sponsor(s)/applicant(s)/organization of said block parties shall meet and adhere to the following guidelines and requirements: 
(1)  No person shall engage in, participate, aid, or organize any block party, unless a block party permit shall be obtained by the city. 
(2)  This article shall not apply to any governmental agency acting within the scope of its functions. In addition, this article does not apply to film production in the city. 
(3)  There shall be paid at the time of filing the application for block party permit a fee of $50.00 that includes processing said application and use of city barricades. 
(4)  The applicant must submit the request for a block party permit at least 14 days prior to the date of the event to allow the police department adequate time to coordinate and process your application. 
(5)  The request will be approved or denied by the city police department and the city fire department within seven days of receipt by the police and fire departments. Applicant/sponsor will be notified if said request was approved or denied. 
(6)  If said request was approved by the city police and fire departments, then said request for permit will be submitted to the mayor and board of aldermen for final approval. Immediately upon the approval for a permit by the city police and fire departments, a copy thereof shall be sent to the following: city clerk; city attorney; and public works director. 
(7)  A block permit will only be issued for a single city block (intersection to intersection). 
(8)  There must be immediate access of the surrounding area for emergency personnel and apparatus at all times. 
(9)  Public works will deliver barricades to the applicant's residence in time for the event. Barricades will be picked up at the applicant's residence on the following business day after the event. 
(10)  Applicant is responsible for placing barricades at the entrance and exit points of the street closure, and for removing barricades upon the deadline of the event. 
(11)  Applicant is responsible for the repair and or replacement of any lost, stolen or damaged barricades furnished to the applicant for the block party. 
(12)  Applicant assumes the responsibility of cleaning up and removing all debris from the designated area upon the deadline of the event. 
(13)  Businesses and neighbors have the right to enjoy peace and quiet at their property. Any disruption will be evaluated by the city police department to determine an appropriate remedy. This form of remedy could include, revocation of the block party. 
(14)  Applicant shall notify the city police department when the designated street has been barricaded and when it is re-opened. 
(15)  Contents of application for permit. An application for a permit for a block party shall set forth the following information: 
a.  Name, address and telephone number of the sponsor(s), applicant(s), or organization seeking to conduct a block party. 
b.  The name, address and telephone number who will be the block party chairman and who will be responsible for its conduct. 
c.  If the block party is proposed to be conducted for an organization, the name, address and telephone number of the headquarters of the organization, and of the authorized and responsible heads of such organization. 
d.  The date when the block party is to be conducted. 
e.  The location of the block party (block from intersection to intersection). 
f.  The approximate number of persons who will be attending the block party. 
g.  What type of entertainment will be provided? 
h.  The hours when the block party will start and terminate. 
i.  Any other information that the police and or fire chiefs shall find reasonably necessary to make a fair determination as to whether a permit should be issued. 
j.  An acknowledgement by the applicant/sponsor/organization that they agree to hold harmless the City of Canton, its officials, officers, employees and agents from all suits, actions, damages, or claims to which the city may be subjected to of any kind or nature whatsoever resulting from, caused by arising out of or as a consequence of such temporary street closure and the activities permitted in connection therewith. 
(16)  A block party permit may be denied or revoked for any of the following reasons: 
a.  The conduct of the block party interrupts the safe and orderly movement of traffic contiguous to its location. 
b.  The conduct of the block party will not require the diversion of so great a number of emergency responders of the city as to prevent normal protection of the city. 
c.  The concentration of persons and vehicles at the location of the block party will not unduly interfere with proper fire and police protection of, or ambulance service to, areas contiguous to the assembly area. 
d.  Failure to submit the Block Party Neighbor Agreement form with the appropriate signatures. 
e.  Incomplete application, traffic control issues, issues related to other permits or city mayor and board of aldermen approved events in the city, and other public safety concerns. 
(Ord. of 6-21-16) 
Editor's note— An ordinance adopted June 21, 2016, did not specify manner of inclusion; hence, inclusion as section 22-16.1 is at the discretion of the editor.  
Sec. 22-16.2. - Public indecency. 
(a)  Purpose. It is hereby found and determined that the conduct prohibited by this section is indecent and that such conduct violates the community standards of the city. Likewise, it is found and determined that wearing pants or skirts four inches below the top of the hip is hazardous both to the person wearing the garment and to the general public, as walking when pants and/or skirts are below the top of the hip increases the likelihood of tripping and falling, and injuring oneself or others in the process. Hence, this section is adopted in furtherance of the city's police powers, in the interest of health, sanitation and overall welfare of the community. 
(b)  Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section shall have the meanings as defined in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates otherwise: 
Lewd means obscene, lustful, lascivious, lecherous. The term imports a lascivious intent. It signifies that form of immortality which as relation to moral impurity or that which is carried on in a wanton manner. 
(c)  Public indecency. It shall be unlawful for any person to willfully perform any of the following acts in a place where a person should reasonably expect to be in view of public: 
(1)  A lewd caress or indecent fondling of the sexual organs of any person, including oneself; 
(2)  Public urination or defecation; or 
(3)  Intentionally wearing pants or skirts four inches below the top of the hip (crest of the ilium) and exposing the skin or undergarments. 
(c)  Fines. A fine shall be issue to the offender and the person shall be subject to a fine of not less than $50.00, and not more than $250.00 plus any assessments. In addition to the fine, the city municipal court may order such person to participate in up to 25 hours of court approved community service activities. Violators shall not be subject to arrest or imprisonment for violation of this section, however, the city municipal court shall have full authority to enforce its orders, judgments and sentences. 
(d)  Defenses. It is a defense under this section if it is determined, after a hearing or trial, that the person was exercising rights protected by the federal or state constitution. Any defense under this section must be asserted prior to any hearing or trial in the matter. 
(Ord. of 3-21-17) 
Editor's note— An ordinance adopted March 21, 2017, did not specify manner of inclusion; hence, inclusion as section 22-16.2 is at the discretion of the editor.  
ARTICLE II. - OFFENSES AGAINST PERSONS 
 
Sec. 22-17. - Assaults, menacing threats. 
It shall be unlawful for any person within this city to assault or threaten another in a menacing manner or strike or injure another. 
State Law reference— Assault and battery generally, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 2011 et seq.  
Sec. 22-18. - Provoking assault. 
It shall be unlawful for any person within the city to intentionally provoke or attempt to provoke an assault upon himself or another by the uttering of vile or insulting epithets applied to the assailed party or one so attempting to commit an assault, or to cause or swear at a person or use vile names or slander or abuse the character of another person with the intention of provoking an assault by said person.  
Sec. 22-19. - Molesting minor. 
Any person who shall contribute to or encourage or procure a minor to violate the law; or who shall take indecent or improper liberties with such minor; or who shall expose his or her private parts to such minor in an obscene or indecent manner; or who shall by language, sign or touching such minor, suggest or refer to any lewd, lascivious or indecent act; or who shall detain or divert such minor with intent to perpetrate any of the aforesaid acts; shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor. 
State Law reference— Violation of children, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 2052.  
Secs. 22-20—22-29. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE III. - OFFENSES AGAINST PROPERTY 
 
Sec. 22-30. - Malicious mischief. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to wilfully, mischievously or maliciously destroy, disfigure or injure any property not his own, either real or personal, or any public or private property within the city. 
(Ord. of 2-5-63, § 1) 
State Law reference— Malicious mischief, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 2281.  
Sec. 22-31. - Water towers, poles, similar structures; climbing. 
It shall be unlawful for any person, not employed to do so, to climb or ascend any water tower, elevated water tank or standpipe, telephone, telegraph, electric light or any other publicly or privately owned pole or tower in the city.  
Secs. 22-32—22-41. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE IV. - OFFENSES AGAINST PEACE 
 
Sec. 22-42. - Disturbing the peace. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to commit any offense which shall constitute a disturbance of the family, disturbance of the public peace or disturbance of the peace of others as provided by state law. 
State Law reference— Disturbing the peace, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 2088 et seq.  
Secs. 22-43—22-52. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE V. - WEAPONS[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Deadly weapons generally, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, §§ 2079—2086. 
 
Sec. 22-53. - Discharge of firearms. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to fire or discharge any gun, pistol, cannon, or firearm of any description in the city without a permit from the mayor.  
Sec. 22-54. - Carrying concealed. 
Any person who carries concealed in whole or in part any bowie knife, dirk knife, butcher knife, switchblade knife, metallic knuckles, blackjack, slingshot, pistol, revolver, or any rifle with a barrel of less than 16 inches in length, or any shotgun with a barrel of less than 18 inches in length, machine gun or any fully automatic firearm or other deadly weapon, or any muffler or silencer for any firearm, whether or not it is accompanied by a firearm shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor. 
State Law reference— Similar state law, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 2079.  
Sec. 22-55. - Throwing missiles. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to throw or propel any stone, gravel, lead or other object or missile by slingshot, hand or otherwise against the house or upon the premises of another or at any person or at any vehicle.  
Sec. 22-56. - Violation of statutes regarding deadly weapons; imposition of maximum penalty. 
Upon a conviction of any individual in violation of §§ 97-37-1 and 97-37-7 of the Mississippi Code of 1972, annotated and as amended, [such individual shall] receive the maximum penalty allowed by law which is within the jurisdiction of the municipal court of the city. 
(Ord. of 7-2-91)  
Secs. 22-57—22-65. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE VI. - PARADES[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Editor's note— An ordinance adopted February 19, 2013, repealed and reenacted article VI in its entirety to read as herein set out. Formerly, article VI, sections 22-66—22-76 pertained to similar subject matter, and derived from original codification, and an ordinance adopted May 2, 1961, §§ 1—3. 
 
Sec. 22-66. - Definitions. 
Applicant shall mean any person or organization who seeks parade permit from the city to conduct or sponsor an event governed by this section. An applicant must be 18 years of age or older. 
Appropriate city officials means the mayor, city clerk, fire chief, police chief and public works director. 
Aldermen means the board of aldermen of the City of Canton, Mississippi. 
Parade means any march, procession or other similar activity consisting of persons, animals, vehicles or things, or combination thereof, upon any public street, sidewalk, alley or other public place or right-of-way, which does not comply with normal and usual traffic regulations or controls. This term does not include a funeral procession. 
(Ord. of 2-19-13)  
Sec. 22-67. - Permit. 
No person shall conduct, sponsor or knowingly participate in a parade unless the mayor and board of aldermen have granted a permit for that parade. 
(Ord. of 2-19-13)  
Sec. 22-68. - Application for permit. 
(a)  Any person who wants to conduct or sponsor a parade must apply to the city clerk for a permit at least 15 days in advance of the date of the parade. The city clerk will refer the application to the appropriate city officials for comments as to whether the application satisfies the findings provided for in section 22-69. 
(b)  The city clerk must receive and process an application for a permit which is filed less than 15 days prior to the date the parade is to occur only if the city clerk determines there is sufficient time to receive comments from the appropriate city officials and to present the application to the aldermen or to individual alderman. 
(c)  An application for a permit must contain the following information, which must be updated by the applicant as circumstances change: 
(1)  Name, address and daytime telephone number of the applicant and, if applicable, the organization with which the applicant is affiliated or on whose behalf the applicant is applying. 
(2)  The date of the proposed parade and the hours that it will commence and terminate. 
(3)  The location and exact street address of the parade assembly and disbanding areas, and the time when the parade will begin to assemble and disband. 
(4)  The approximate number of persons and vehicles, floats or other units to participate in the parade. 
(5)  The route along which the parade will proceed and the sidewalks or lanes of traffic it will occupy; and 
(6)  A list identifying the type and number of all animals the applicant intends to have at the parade. 
(d)  The application must be accompanied by payment of the license fee as established by the aldermen. 
(Ord. of 2-19-13)  
Sec. 22-69. - Issuance of permit. 
(a)  The aldermen must issue a parade permit if it can make those findings listed in subsection (b) of this section. 
(b)  The relevant findings for the issuance of a parade permit are as follows: 
(1)  The proposed parade will not substantially or unnecessarily interfere with traffic in the area contiguous to the activity, or that, if the activity will substantially interfere with such traffic, there are available at the time of the proposed parade sufficient city resources to adequately mitigate the disruption. 
(2)  There will be available at the time of the proposed parade a sufficient number of peace officers, traffic control officials or authorized volunteers to police and protect lawful participants in the parade and non-participants from traffic related hazards in light of the other demands for police protection at the time of the proposed parade. 
(3)  The concentration of persons, animals, vehicles or things at the assembly and disbanding areas and along the parade route will not prevent proper police or fire protection, or ambulance service. 
(4)  The proposed parade will not be conducted for an unlawful purpose or in an unlawful manner. Federal, state and local laws will determine a lawful purpose and a lawful manner. 
(5)  The proposed parade will not interfere with the use of the requested area by another person to whom a valid permit has been issued for the same area or route. 
(6)  The application contains sufficient information about the proposed route and crowd. 
(c)  The aldermen may limit the parade to the sidewalk or to one or more traffic lanes of a street when it determines such limited area is capable of accommodating the number of people anticipated to participate in the parade and the experience of previous comparable parades. The aldermen's action under this subdivision will not be considered a denial of the application for a parade permit. 
Except as otherwise provided by law, all applications for parade permits will be processed on a first-come, first-serve basis. 
(Ord. of 2-19-13)  
Sec. 22-70. - Informal approval. 
If there is no board of aldermen meeting between the time the application is filed with the city clerk and the date of the parade, the city clerk must contact each of the available aldermen to determine whether they can make the findings required in section 22-69. 
The city clerk must inform each alderman contacted of the appropriate city officials' comments. If four aldermen approve of the application, the city clerk must issue a permit to the applicant. 
(Ord. of 2-19-13)  
Sec. 22-71. - Alternate parade permit. 
When the aldermen denies an application for a parade permit, the aldermen may authorize the issuance of a permit for a date, time, location or route that is different from that named by the applicant. This alternate parade permit will, to the extent practicable, authorize an event that will have comparable public visibility and a similar route, location and date to that of the proposed parade. An applicant desiring to accept an alternate parade permit must, within five business days following notice of the aldermen's approval of such a permit, file a written notice of acceptance with the city clerk. 
(Ord. of 2-19-13)  
Sec. 22-72. - Penalty. 
Any person who violates this section is guilty of a misdemeanor and shall pay fine of __________. 
Appeal procedure. 
(1)  The applicant shall have the right to appeal the denial of a permit or a permit condition to the mayor and board of aldermen of the city by the filing of a notice of appeal with the city clerk within ten days of notification of said denial or permit condition. 
(2)  The mayor and board of aldermen shall hold a hearing at the next available regularly scheduled meeting of that body. The decision of the mayor and board of aldermen shall be final. 
(Ord. of 2-19-13)  
Sec. 22-73. - Indemnification agreement. 
Prior to the issuance of a special event permit, the permit applicant or sponsor (if any), must sign an agreement to reimburse the city for any costs incurred by the city in repairing damage to city property occurring in connection with the permitted event proximately caused by the actions of the permittee/sponsoring organization, its officers, employees, or agents, or any person who was under the permittee/sponsoring organizations control insofar as permitted by law. The agreement shall also provide that the permittee/sponsoring organization shall hold harmless, indemnify and defend the city, its officials, members, agents and employees from any claim of injury or damage arising from or proximately caused by actions of the permittee/sponsoring organization, its officers, employees, or agents, or any person who was under the permittee/sponsoring organization's control, in connection with the permitted event, regardless of whether the city is actively negligent or passively negligent, except for those claims, costs, damages, demands, liability and notices, or any of these, caused solely by the negligence or willful misconduct of the city. Persons who merely join in a parade or event are not considered to be "under the control" of the permittee/sponsoring organization by that reason alone. 
(Ord. of 2-19-13)  
Sec. 22-74. - Insurance. 
The applicant/sponsoring organization of an event must possess or obtain public liability insurance to protect against loss from liability imposed by law for damages on account of bodily injury and property damage arising from the event. Such insurance shall name on the policy or by endorsement as additional insureds the city, its officers, employees and agents. Insurance coverage must be maintained for the duration of the event. Coverage shall be a comprehensive general liability insurance policy with the following minimum limits: 
(1)  $_______________ each person—Bodily injury; $_______________ each occurrence Bodily injury; $_______________ each occurrence—Property damage; or 
(2)  $_______________ each occurrence combined single limit bodily injury and property damage. 
a.  A copy of the policy or certificate of insurance along with all necessary endorsements must be filed with the city clerk no less than five days before the date of the event, unless the city clerk for good cause waives the filing deadline. The city clerk permit shall not be issued by the city clerk until after the insurance policy or certificate of insurance, along with necessary endorsements, have been filed by the applicant/sponsor and approved by the city clerk. 
b.  The insurance requirements of subsections (1) and (2) above may be waived by the special events committee for non-athletic events, if the applicant or officer of the sponsoring organization signs a verified statement that he believes the event's purpose is First Amendment expression, and that he has determined that the cost of obtaining insurance is so financially burdensome that it would constitute an unreasonable burden on the right of First Amendment expression. The statement shall include the name and address of one insurance agent or other source for insurance coverage contacted to determine insurance premium rates for insurance coverage. The committee shall review such statement before any determination regarding waiver of insurance. Nothing herein shall waive the requirement to complete the indemnification agreement as required by __________.13 
(Ord. of 2-19-13)  
Secs. 22-75—22-86. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE VII. - DISPOSITION OF LOST, STOLEN, ABANDONED PROPERTY[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
Cross reference— Junk and junk dealers, Ch. 17; police, Ch. 27. 
State Law reference— Disposition of lost, stolen or abandoned personal property, Miss. Code Ann. 1942, § 3374-168. 
 
Sec. 22-87. - Disposal generally. 
Any lost, stolen, abandoned or misplaced personal property held by or otherwise in the custody of the city may be disposed of by the city pursuant to the provisions of Section 3374-168 of the Mississippi Code Annotated, 1942, and the provisions of this article.  
Sec. 22-88. - Claimant to pay city's expense. 
Any person claiming to be the owner of any lost, stolen, abandoned or misplaced personal property held by or in the custody of the city, or claiming the proceeds of sale of any such property pursuant to state law, shall before receiving such property or proceeds pay to the city its reasonable expense of storing and accounting for and dealing with such property.  
Sec. 22-89. - Unsold property. 
If there be no bidder at any sale of personal property authorized by this article, such property shall, after 12 months after the attempted sale thereof, be deemed forfeited and shall be disposed of at the discretion of the mayor and board of aldermen.  
Secs. 22-90—22-99. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE VIII. - CIVIL EMERGENCY CURFEW[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
Cross reference— Mayor, § 2-28 et seq.; civil defense, Ch. 9; closure of alcoholic beverages places of business, § 4-8; floodplain management, Ch. 12½. 
 
Sec. 22-100. - Definitions. 
(a)  A civil emergency is hereby defined to be: 
(1)  A riot or unlawful assembly characterized by the use of actual force or violence or any threat to use force if accompanied by immediate power to execute by three or more persons acting together without authority of law. 
(2)  Any natural disaster or man-made calamity including flood, conflagration, cyclone, tornado, earthquake or explosion within the corporate limits of the city resulting in the death or injury of persons or the destruction of property to such an extent that extraordinary measures must be taken to protect the public health, safety and welfare. 
(b)  Curfew is hereby defined as a prohibition against any person or persons walking, running, loitering, standing, or motoring upon any alley, street, highway, public property or vacant premises within the corporate limits of the city, excepting persons officially designated to duty with reference to said civil emergency.  
Sec. 22-101. - Declaration. 
When in the judgment of the mayor or mayor pro tem, a civil emergency is deemed to exist within the city, the mayor or mayor pro tem shall forthwith proclaim in writing the existence of same.  
Sec. 22-102. - Imposition of curfew. 
After the proclamation of a civil emergency by the mayor or mayor pro tem, the mayor or mayor pro tem may order a general curfew applicable to such geographical areas of the city or to the city as a whole, as the mayor or mayor pro tem deems advisable, and applicable during such hours of the day or night as the mayor or mayor pro tem deems necessary in the interest of the public safety and welfare.  
Sec. 22-103. - Same—Restriction of activities. 
After the proclamation of a civil emergency, the mayor or the mayor pro tem may also in the interest of public safety and welfare make any or all of the following orders: 
(a)  Order the closing of all retail liquor stores. 
(b)  Order the closing of all beer taverns. 
(c)  Order the closing of all private clubs or portions thereof wherein the consumption of intoxicating liquor or beer is permitted. 
(d)  Order the discontinuance of the sale of beer. 
(e)  Order the discontinuance of selling, distributing or giving away gasoline or other liquid flammable or combustible products in any container other than a gasoline tank properly affixed to a motor vehicle. 
(f)  Order the closing of gasoline stations and other establishments, the chief activity of which is the sale, distribution or dispensing of liquid flammable or combustible products. 
(g)  Order the discontinuance of selling, distributing, dispensing or giving away of any firearms or ammunition of any character whatsoever. 
(h)  Order the closing of any or all establishments or portions thereof, the chief activity of which is the sale, distribution, dispensing or giving away of firearms or ammunition. 
(i)  Issue such other orders as are imminently necessary for the protection of life and property.  
Secs. 22-104—22-120. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE IX. - FLEA MARKET DAYS[5] 

Footnotes: 
--- (5) --- 
Editor's note— An ordinance of April 1, 1986, did not specifically amend the Code; therefore, inclusion of §§ 1 through 18 of the aforesaid ordinance as §§ 22-121 through 22-138 was at the discretion of the editor. This article shall be effective from and after April 1, 1986. 
 
Sec. 22-121. - Definition. 
The Canton Flea Market is an arts and crafts show which is sponsored by the City of Canton and the Madison County Chamber of Commerce at designated times each year. 
(Ord. of 4-1-86, § 1)  
Sec. 22-122. - Days designated. 
The second Thursday of May and the second Thursday of October each year are hereby designated as Flea Market Days. 
(Ord. of 4-1-86, § 2)  
Sec. 22-123. - Permits. 
Flea market permits of four types may be granted by the City of Canton as follows: 
Type  I. Allowing the sale of food and/or beverage. 
Type  II. Allowing the sale of arts, crafts and plants in flea market Zone A as hereinafter described. 
Type III. Allowing the sale of arts, crafts, goods, wares, merchandise and plants in flea market Zones B or C as hereinafter described. Said permits shall be individually referred to as type III-B or type III-C. 
(Ord. of 4-1-86, § 3)  
Sec. 22-124. - Management committee. 
(a)  Members. The flea market management committee shall be appointees of the mayor and board of aldermen and shall consist of a representative from the following public bodies: 
(1)  Canton Municipal Utilities; 
(2)  Canton Convention and Visitors Bureau; 
(3)  Madison County Historical Society; 
(4)  Canton Flea Market, Inc.; and 
(5)  Canton Chamber of Commerce/Main Street Association. 
(b)  Function. The function of said committee shall be to oversee the issuance of permits and to oversee the overall operation of the Canton Flea Market and the operation by such permittees. The flea market management committee shall have the invested authority to govern and oversee the flea market. It shall elect officers, set and schedule meetings, develop policy and conduct general business, following Robert's Rules of Order, as it relates to the flea market. 
(c)  Authority. The flea market management committee shall have the authority to appoint an ad hoc committee to hear, or shall have the full committee to hear, any reasonable complaint from a vendor who has been grieved, accused of violating the rules, regulations, and policy of the flea market, or who has been ousted from the flea market for a just or non-just cause. The time for response and final decision shall be set by the flea market management committee. 
(d)  Right to appeal. Anyone aggrieved by any decision of the flea market management committee shall have the right to appeal said decision to the mayor and board of aldermen. Any such individual shall be informed of his right to appeal. A request for appellate review must be made, in writing, by the aggrieved individual within 30 days from the final decision by the flea market management committee. Final judgment by the mayor and board of aldermen of the city constitutes the exhaustion of administrative remedies by any aggrieved party. The parties shall also be made aware of his rights to legal recourse 
(Ord. of 4-186, § 4; Ord. of 9-15-98)  
Sec. 22-125. - Zones. 
(a)  Flea market permits type II and type III shall not be granted except to persons or business which shall exhibit in the flea market zones A, B or C as referred to in section 22-123 above and described as follows: 
The following described real property lying and being situated in the city: 
Zone A. The City of Canton Courthouse Square, as well as the portions of Union Street and Center Street, which establish the north and west boundaries thereof, excluding the area within the store front sidewalks and parking spaces fronting said sidewalks. 
Zone B. Lot 16 on the north side of East Fulton Street and Lots 17 and 19 on the south side of East Fulton Street. 
Zone C. 
Part 1. All that property which lies 70 feet north of and 70 feet south of the center line of that portion of East Peace Street which begins 200 feet east of its intersection with Liberty Street and runs easterly to a point which is 300 feet west of the point of intersection of the center lines of East Peace Street and Lyon Street. Also, all of Lots 24, 26, 33, 35, 38 and East ½ of Lot 40, not heretofore included. 
Part 2. All that property which lies 55 feet north of and 55 feet south of the center line of that portion of East Fulton Street which begins at its intersection with South Liberty Street and runs easterly to its intersection with Lyon Street, also all of Lot 25 on the south side of East Fulton Street and Lots 2 and 4 on the east side of Lyon Street. Less and except any portion of the subject property which is located in zone B. 
Part 3. All that property which lies 70 feet east of the center line of that portion of South Liberty Street which begins at East Peace Street and runs southerly to its intersection with East Fulton Street. Less and except, from Zones B and C, any portion of the subject property in street rights-of-way. 
Zone D. 
Part 1. All that property bounded on the north by West Peace Street, on the east by Hickory Street, on the south by Fulton Street, and on the west by the Illinois Central Railroad tracks. 
Part 2. All businesses fronting on that portion of West Peace Street from its intersection with Union Street in a westerly direction to its intersection with the Illinois Central Railroad. 
Part 3. All that property which lies 70 feet east of and 70 feet west of the center line of that portion of North Hickory Street from its intersection with West Peace Street in a northerly direction to its intersection with West Center Street Extended. 
(b)  That flea market zone A which shall be strictly controlled by the Canton Flea Market, Inc. That flea market zone B shall be strictly controlled by the Madison County Historical Society, except for spaces reserved for type I permits. That flea market zone C shall be strictly controlled by a flea market zone C committee which shall be composed of six persons which own real property within zone C, with preference being given to property owners who lease spaces and/or have exhibits on flea market days, and one representative of the Canton Flea Market Inc. The Fulton Street and Rings property homeowners, as well as the Madison County Historical Society, will name and appoint members of the flea market zone C committee, subject to approval thereof by the mayor. That flea market zone D shall be strictly controlled by the Madison County Cultural Arts Coalition. 
(c)  In addition, any local business establishment possessing a proper privilege license, which is located on the portions of Union Street and Center Street which form the north and west boundaries of the Canton Courthouse Square, may utilize that portion of the sidewalk and marked parking spaces directly adjacent to such business establishment to conduct the business for which said privilege license was issued or for any type I permit issued. 
(Ord. of 4-1-86, § 5; Ord. of 9-1-98)  
Sec. 22-126. - Sale of goods. 
On flea market days the exhibit of and/or sale of arts, crafts, goods, wares, merchandise, plants, food or beverages of any type is prohibited except by local business establishments possessing proper privilege licenses and except by those persons and/or businesses which have obtained a proper flea market permit from the City of Canton. Garage sales, carport sales and those similar in nature are prohibited on flea market days. 
(Ord. of 4-1-86, § 6)  
Sec. 22-127. - Application. 
(a)  The application for a flea market permit required by the provisions hereof, the form and contents of which have been approved by the City of Canton, shall be procured from the Canton City Hall, Canton, Mississippi, and shall be completed in full, providing all information and materials requested, and returned to the office of the city clerk for processing, together with a permit fee in the amount of $10.00 for a type I permit, $140.00 for a type II permit and $140.00 for a type III permit. 
(b)  For any person or business who exhibited at the previous market, no permit will be issued unless said exhibitor filed a Mississippi State Sales Tax Report reflecting sales at said previous market. 
(Ord. of 4-1-86, § 7; Ord. of 8-19-86; Ord. of 5-7-91; Ord. of 4-19-94)  
Sec. 22-128. - Issuance of type II and type III permits. 
(a)  No type II flea market permit shall be issued by the city unless: 
(1)  The applicant acknowledges that he (she) has received a copy of the flea market guidelines and agrees in writing to comply with applicable guidelines. 
(2)  The city clerk receives a written recommendation from the chamber of commerce that a flea market permit be issued to the applicant. 
(b)  No type III-B flea market permit shall be issued by the city unless: 
(1)  The applicant acknowledges in writing that he (she) has received a copy of the flea market guidelines and agrees in writing to comply with applicable guidelines. 
(2)  The city clerk receives a written recommendation from the Madison County Historical Society that a flea market permit be issued to the applicant. 
(c)  No type III-C flea market permit shall be issued by the city unless: 
(1)  The applicant acknowledges in writing that he (she) has received a copy of the flea market guidelines and agrees in writing to comply with applicable guidelines. 
(2)  The city clerk receives a written recommendation from the individual property owner, from which the applicant will lease a space, that a flea market permit be issued to the applicant. 
(Ord. of 4-1-86, § 8)  
Sec. 22-129. - Location of space. 
The application shall contain a description of the location where the applicant proposes to operate. No type II flea market permit shall be issued to conduct business except in flea market zone A. No type III-B flea market permit shall be issued to conduct business except in flea market zone B and no type III-C flea market permit shall be issued to conduct business except in flea market zone C. 
(Ord. of 4-1-86, § 9)  
Sec. 22-130. - Food and beverages. 
(a)  No food or beverage shall be served or sold in the City of Canton on flea market days except by local persons or businesses which possess proper privilege licenses and are regularly engaged in the sale of same and except by those organizations which obtain a type I flea market permit. 
(b)  Type I permits shall be issued only to local civic groups, nonprofit and/or religious organizations unless an insufficient number of such organizations as determined by the flea market management committee apply for type I permits to meet the needs of those expected to attend any given flea market. 
(c)  No type I flea market permit shall be issued by the city unless: 
(1)  The city clerk receives a written notification from the flea market management committee that the said applicant has been presented with a copy of such flea market guidelines. 
(2)  The applicant acknowledges receipt of said flea market guidelines and agrees in writing to comply with applicable flea market guidelines. 
(3)  The city clerk receives a written recommendation from the flea market management committee that a flea market permit be issued to the applicant. 
(Ord. of 4-1-86, § 10)  
Sec. 22-131. - Contents of permit. 
Each flea market permit issued under the provisions hereof shall state the name, address and telephone number of the permittee as well as the location where the permittee will exhibit. The permit shall be signed by the city clerk, and it shall state the date of issuance and the date upon which such permit shall be used. Any permit not dated and signed as herein provided, or which was issued in violation hereof, shall be void. Type I permits shall also include provisions describing the type foods and/or beverages to be sold, the number of booths allowed. 
(Ord. of 4-1-86, § 11)  
Sec. 22-132. - Display of permit. 
Every receipt of a flea market permit shall display said permit in a conspicuous place at the location where business is conducted. 
(Ord. of 4-1-86, § 12)  
Sec. 22-133. - Liability. 
The City of Canton and the Madison County Chamber of Commerce shall have no liability or responsibility for injury of any type suffered by persons on private property within the City of Canton. Each property owner should provide his own liability protection. 
(Ord. of 4-1-86, § 13)  
Sec. 22-134. - Cleanup. 
Each permittee shall cause the area in which the permittee exhibits or sells to be maintained in a neat and clean manner during the course of the flea market and at the conclusion the permittee shall cause all trash, debris and litter in and immediately around permittee's location to be picked up and removed or stored at the site in garbage bags and/or boxes. 
(Ord. of 4-1-86, § 14)  
Sec. 22-135. - Inspection. 
The respective committees shall inspect the operations of all permittees during the course of each flea market to ensure compliance with flea market guidelines and this article, and the committees shall within 30 days after each flea market day provide each noncomplying permittee with the details of any noncompliance, and a copy of such noncompliance report shall be provided to the city clerk. 
Any noncompliance shall be grounds for refusal to issue any flea market permit to the noncomplying party for a period of three years from the date of such noncompliance. 
(Ord. of 4-1-86, § 15)  
Sec. 22-136. - Duration of permit. 
Every flea market permit issued pursuant to the provisions hereof shall entitle the recipient to conduct business for a period of one day on the designated flea market day. 
(Ord. of 4-1-86, § 16)  
Sec. 22-137. - Revocation of permit. 
Any flea market permit issued under the provisions of this article may be revoked for the violation by the recipient of any provisions of this article, flea market guidelines, state law or city ordinance, and upon such revocation such permit shall be immediately surrendered to the city clerk, and failure to do so shall constitute a misdemeanor. 
(Ord. of 4-1-86, § 17)  
Sec. 22-138. - Penalty. 
Failure to comply with any provisions hereof shall constitute a misdemeanor. Any person or entity found guilty of violating this article shall be subject to a fine not exceeding $500.00 or imprisonment not exceeding 90 days, or both. 
(Ord. of 4-1-86, § 18)  
Sec. 22-139. - Sales tax to be collected. 
Any sponsor of any exhibitor at any future Canton Flea Market Arts & Crafts Show shall collect from said exhibitor the appropriate Mississippi State sales tax return, as well as any sales taxes due and owing, and to deliver same to the city clerk, on or before the close of business on the Friday following each flea market. 
(Ord. of 9-2-08) 
Editor's note— An ordinance adopted September 2, 2008, did not specify manner of inclusion; hence, inclusion as section 22-139 is at the discretion of the editor.  
Secs. 22-140—22-155. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE X. - CURFEW FOR MINORS[6] 

Footnotes: 
--- (6) --- 
Editor's note— Sections 1—7 of an ordinance adopted April 7, 1998, did not specifically amend the Code and have been included herein as superseding the provisions of former Art. X, relative to the presence and conduct of minors on streets and other public places, which derived from §§ 1—8 of an ordinance adopted July 2, 1991. 
 
Sec. 22-156. - Title. 
This article shall be known as the "curfew ordinance". 
(Ord. of 4-7-98, § 1)  
Sec. 22-157. - Purpose and findings. 
(a)  The board of aldermen have determined that juveniles are known to congregate at late and unusual hours of the night in public and private places without the supervision of their parents or other responsible adults and during hours when schools are in session and in violation of the Mississippi Compulsory School Attendance Law. 
(b)  The board of aldermen believes that by regulating the behavior of juveniles through the curfew ordinance, crime in the city will be positively impacted and parents will be held more accountable for their minor children. 
(Ord. of 4-7-98, § 2)  
Sec. 22-158. - Definitions. 
The following terms, phrases and words shall have the meaning as given below: 
City is the City of Canton. 
Establishment means any privately owned place of business operated for profit to which the public is invited, including any place of entertainment or amusement. 
Minor or juvenile for the purposes of this article shall mean any person who has not reached his/her eighteenth birthday. 
Parent is any person who has legal custody of a minor, whether that person be the natural or adoptive parent; legal guardian or a person who has been given legal custody through a court order. 
Permit means to knowingly allow or knowingly fail to prevent; or fail to prevent supervision due to lack of reasonable efforts. 
Police shall mean the Canton Police Department. 
Street is a way or place designed for use of the public for vehicular travel. 
(Ord. of 4-7-98, § 3)  
Sec. 22-159. - Restrictions. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any minor to be present on any public street, park, vacant lot, establishment or other place during the period beginning at 11:00 p.m. and ending at 6:00 a.m. on each day of the week. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any compulsory school age child or minor up to age 17 who has not reached his/her eighteenth birthday to be present on any public street, park, vacant lot, establishment or other place during the following period: 
From 8:45 a.m. until 2:15 p.m. during the period when the Mississippi Compulsory School Attendance Law (Section 37-13-91) is in effect. 
(c)  It shall be unlawful for a parent of a minor child to knowingly permit such minor to be present on any street or establishment beyond the scope of this article as delineated in subsections (a) and (b) above. For the purpose of this article, "knowingly" includes knowledge that a parent should possess regarding the activities and whereabouts of his/her minor child. 
(d)  It shall be unlawful for the owner, operator, or any employee of an establishment to permit a minor to be present on the premises of the establishment during curfew hours delineated in subsections (a) and (b). 
(Ord. of 4-7-98, § 4)  
Sec. 22-160. - Exceptions. 
The following shall be exceptions to the provisions of this curfew ordinance: 
(1)  Any time that a minor is accompanied by his/her parent. 
(2)  When a minor is accompanied by an adult designated by the parent to oversee or take charge of the minor for a specified period, purpose and area. 
(3)  When the minor is on a verifiable errand for his/her parent. 
(4)  If the minor is legally employed and traveling directly to his/her place of employment or directly from his/her place of employment and en route to his/her home. 
(5)  When a minor is returning home from a school or religious function he/she shall be allowed one hour from the time the event ends to arrive at home. (Note: Most school events are over by 10:00 or 10:30 p.m. Therefore, minors usually will be required to return home between 11:00 and 11:30 p.m. 
(6)  When a minor is dispatched by his/her parent on an errand involving necessity; i.e., drug store for medicine, grocery store for items for infant child, etc., he/she will not be picked up. 
(7)  When a minor who has verifiable parental consent to be in a motor vehicle engaged in legitimate interstate travel through the city. 
(8)  This article shall not apply to 17-year-old members of the Armed Forces. 
(9)  Each of the foregoing exceptions and their several limitations are severable, as hereinafter provided. 
(Ord. of 4-7-98, § 5)  
Sec. 22-161. - Violations. 
(a)  A police officer of the city who has probable cause to believe that a minor is in violation of the curfew ordinance shall conduct a complete investigation and prepare the necessary reports. 
(b)  Notwithstanding the above, a police officer who has probable cause to believe that the minor is in violation of this article, shall transport the minor to the police department or another authorized location. 
(c)  When a minor is taken to the police department or another authorized location, the minor's parent(s) or legal guardian shall be immediately contacted. If after this contact there is still probable cause to believe that the minor was violating this article, the minor shall be held until the parent(s) or legal guardian comes to take the minor home. When the parent(s) or legal guardian arrives, he or she shall be given a copy of this article.
